# Platform Replication Landscape

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## Purpose

This document maps the comparable companies across each product layer KaNeXT spans. The reader draws their own conclusion about replication cost.

KaNeXT is not one company. KaNeXT is ten product families integrated into one governed architecture. To replicate what one founder has built would require acquiring and integrating companies across sports intelligence, institutional operating systems, AI interface layers, streaming, payments and fintech, real-time stats, video intelligence, gaming, sensor hardware, and governance and compliance.

No single comparable exists. The fragmented market across these layers tells the story.

All valuations and market capitalizations referenced are from public filings and reporting as of April 2026 where available.

---

## Layer 1: Sports Intelligence

KaNeXT intelligence scope: 27+ sport-specific domains, 250,000+ athlete database, league governance across 15+ amateur and professional leagues, NIL intelligence, market and betting intelligence, Smart Ball hardware intelligence across 9 sports, KLVN normalization across competitive levels, simulation engines, scouting frameworks, team intelligence, and player development intelligence.

### Hudl (Sports Video Analysis)

Hudl is the dominant video analysis platform in sports, founded 2006. It provides video capture, tagging, and review tools used by more than 153,000 active teams across basketball, football, soccer, and other sports.

**Funding and structure:** Private. $230M total raised across 6 rounds. Most recent round: Bain Capital Tech Opportunities growth investment (2020, financial terms undisclosed). Additional stakeholders include Accel, Nelnet, and Vista Equity Partners. 3,500 employees. Acquisitions completed 2024-2025 include StatsBomb (August 2024), Balltime (February 2025), FastModel Sports (March 2025), and Titan Sports (June 2025), expanding Hudl into analytics, wearables, and performance tracking.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Hudl does video and analytics for multiple sports. KaNeXT does intelligence (player evaluation, team construction, simulation, governance) at architectural depth that video platforms do not reach. Hudl's core product is video storage and tagging; KaNeXT's is governed intelligence reasoning. Hudl has built to multi-sport breadth through acquisitions; KaNeXT built to 27+ sports through unified architecture.

### Sportradar Group

Sportradar provides sports data services for the betting and media industries. It collects, packages, and distributes real-time sports data globally.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $4.5-5B (April 2026). Trailing twelve-month revenue $1.45B. 2025 revenue grew 17% to €1,290M.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Sportradar is a B2B sports data infrastructure business primarily serving betting operators. KaNeXT's market and betting intelligence is one of 10+ product families. Sportradar does not do player evaluation, institutional intelligence, NIL, team operating systems, payments, or hardware. Sportradar is the market infrastructure layer; KaNeXT includes a comparable layer as one component.

### Genius Sports

Genius Sports provides sports technology across three areas: sports technology and services, betting technology and content, and media technology. It partners with leagues including the NFL and NBA for official data distribution.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $1.1-1.5B (April 2026). TTM revenue $669M. Focused on data distribution, betting, and media infrastructure.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Comparable to Sportradar but smaller. Same scope characterization. One layer, not the full stack.

### Catapult Sports

Catapult provides wearable performance-tracking technology used by professional and college sports teams for athlete monitoring.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $684M (April 2026). TTM revenue $126M. Focused on sensor wearables and performance data.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Catapult is a pure-play wearables hardware plus analytics company. KaNeXT's Smart Ball architecture spans 9 ball sports with integrated intelligence. Catapult is one narrow slice (wearables on the body) of what KaNeXT covers (ball sensors plus wearables plus camera vision plus unified intelligence).

### Stats Perform

Stats Perform provides sports data, content, AI, and technology to media companies, leagues, and betting operators.

**Acquisition:** Acquired by Vista Equity Partners at approximately $2.3B enterprise value.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Multi-sport data and content distribution. Similar characterization to Sportradar and Genius Sports. One layer, not the full stack.

### Teamworks

Teamworks is the Operating System for Sports, powering 6,500+ teams globally. Through acquisitions (INFLCR for NIL, ARMS Software for compliance, Smartabase for performance, Zelus Analytics for sports intelligence, Telemetry Sports for analytics, Basepath for NIL), Teamworks has assembled a sports operations platform.

**Private company:** Raised $235M Series F in June 2025 at pre-money valuation exceeding $1.0B, led by Dragoneer Investment Group. Serves 100% of NFL teams, 99% of Division I NCAA athletic departments, 90% of MLB and Premier League, 87% of NBA, 83% of MLS, 81% of NHL, and 65+ Olympic federations across 24 countries.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Teamworks is the closest comparable in scope ambition. Teamworks has assembled its stack through acquisitions (INFLCR + ARMS + Smartabase + Zelus + Telemetry + Basepath) while KaNeXT built its stack from unified architecture by one founder. Teamworks does athlete operations, NIL management, communication, compliance, performance, and acquired sports analytics (Zelus). KaNeXT extends into institutional operations beyond athletics (5 modes vs Athletics-only), payments (KPay), streaming (KTV), stats (KStat), video intelligence (KVision), gaming (KPlay), hardware (Smart Ball), enrollment engine, AI interface layer (Dipson), and 27 institutional intelligence modules across People and Talent, Operations and Infrastructure, Leadership and Governance, Growth and External, and Finance and Assets. At valuation of $1B+ for Teamworks's narrower scope and assembled architecture, the comparable establishes a floor for sports operations platforms at KaNeXT's ambition level.

### Sports Intelligence Layer Summary

| Company | Valuation | Revenue | Scope |
|---|---|---|---|
| Hudl | Private, $230M raised, Bain-backed | Undisclosed | Video analysis across multiple sports, expanding into analytics |
| Sportradar | ~$4.5-5B market cap | $1.45B TTM | Sports data infrastructure for betting and media |
| Genius Sports | ~$1.1-1.5B market cap | $669M TTM | Sports data and betting technology |
| Catapult Sports | ~$684M market cap | $126M TTM | Wearables and performance analytics |
| Stats Perform | Acquired ~$2.3B | - | Data, content, and AI for sports |
| Teamworks | Private, $1B+ (2025) | Undisclosed | Operating system for sports teams; multiple acquisitions |

Aggregate sports intelligence layer market cap or valuation: approximately $10-15B across the fragmented companies each covering portions of what KaNeXT covers within one product family.

---

## Layer 2: Institutional Operating Systems

KaNeXT institutional operating system scope: 5 modes (Personal, Business, Education, Community, Athletics), 9 tiles per mode, Universal RBAC with 7 roles, 4,500+ line OS Mode Specification, and 27 institutional intelligence modules organized across People and Talent, Operations and Infrastructure, Leadership and Governance, Growth and External, and Finance and Assets.

### Workday

Workday provides enterprise cloud applications for human capital management, financial management, and business planning for enterprises including higher education institutions.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $30B (April 2026). Trailing twelve-month revenue $9.6B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Workday is the dominant enterprise HR and finance OS. Used by enterprises including hundreds of higher education institutions. KaNeXT's Education Mode covers similar functional scope (institutional administration, student lifecycle, financial operations) but extends to athletics, media, commerce, communications, and community layers that Workday does not address. Workday is one mode of scope at institutional depth; KaNeXT is five modes.

### PowerSchool

PowerSchool is the dominant K-12 education operating system, supporting over 60 million students and 18,000 customers in 90+ countries.

**Acquisition:** Acquired by Bain Capital in October 2024 at $5.6B enterprise value. Previously public (NYSE: PWSC) since 2021.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** PowerSchool is K-12-focused. KaNeXT Education Mode covers higher education and institutional operations at comparable architectural depth but with AI-native interaction via Dipson and integration with athletic, media, and financial layers. PowerSchool demonstrates that the education operating system category commands $5B+ valuations at scale.

### Ellucian

Ellucian is a higher-education focused enterprise software provider serving colleges and universities with student information systems, finance, and human resources software.

**Private company:** Previously valued at approximately $3.5B under various private ownership structures.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Direct higher-education comparable. Ellucian does SIS and admin systems. KaNeXT does SIS-equivalent functions plus athletic operations, media, commerce, payments, intelligence, and community functions. Ellucian is one slice of Education Mode; KaNeXT is the full stack.

### Institutional Operating Systems Layer Summary

| Company | Valuation | Scope |
|---|---|---|
| Workday | ~$30B market cap | Enterprise HR, finance, planning |
| PowerSchool | $5.6B acquisition (2024) | K-12 education OS |
| Ellucian | ~$3.5B private | Higher education SIS |
| Salesforce | ~$250B+ market cap | Enterprise CRM and cloud |
| Microsoft 365 | Component of $3T+ Microsoft | Enterprise productivity |

Aggregate institutional operating systems layer valuation: hundreds of billions in market cap across the category. KaNeXT does not replace all enterprise software; KaNeXT's mode architecture demonstrates comparable governed institutional operations at multi-mode depth that no individual comparable spans.

---

## Layer 3: AI Intelligence Infrastructure

KaNeXT intelligence architecture comparable scope: governed AI reasoning infrastructure across institutional and sport domains, with Dipson as the AI interface layer routing to 50+ skill files.

### Palantir Technologies

Palantir builds governed intelligence operating systems for government and enterprise clients. Foundry (commercial) and Gotham (government) platforms make data operationally useful inside large organizations.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $350B (April 2026). TTM revenue approximately $3.4-4B. Cumulative R&D investment since founding (2003) estimated at $4.5-6B. 2025 R&D expense: $558M.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Palantir is the structural parallel for governed intelligence infrastructure. Palantir builds horizontal intelligence platforms for government and enterprise across industries. KaNeXT builds vertical intelligence across sports and educational institutions, with the same governed-intelligence architectural philosophy. Palantir's $350B market cap demonstrates what the market assigns to governed intelligence operating systems. KaNeXT covers ground Palantir does not (sports, NIL, athletics operations, league governance) and Palantir covers ground KaNeXT does not (defense, enterprise, logistics). The structural comparison establishes that governed intelligence infrastructure commands premium valuations; it does not imply equivalence in scale or category.

### Databricks

Databricks provides a data intelligence platform combining data warehousing and AI workloads.

**Private company:** Valued at approximately $62B in most recent funding rounds.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Data platform infrastructure, not domain-specific intelligence. Comparable in category (AI infrastructure) but different in application (horizontal data platform vs vertical sports and institutional intelligence).

### Snowflake

Snowflake provides a cloud data platform for data warehousing and analytics.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $55-65B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Data warehousing infrastructure, not intelligence layer. Different category.

### AI Intelligence Infrastructure Layer Summary

| Company | Valuation | Scope |
|---|---|---|
| Palantir | ~$350B market cap | Governed intelligence for government and enterprise |
| Databricks | ~$62B private | Data intelligence platform |
| Snowflake | ~$55-65B market cap | Cloud data platform |

Aggregate AI intelligence infrastructure market cap: $450-475B+ across the category. KaNeXT applies the governed intelligence architecture to vertical sports and institutional domains, a category without established pure-play public comparables.

---

## Layer 4: Live Streaming Platform (KTV)

KaNeXT KTV scope: live streaming platform with content library, advertising infrastructure, and integrated channel capability for every platform institution.

### Hudl TV (subset of Hudl)

Hudl acquired BlueFrame Technology to expand livestreaming capability and has integrated streaming across its platform.

**Value embedded:** Included in Hudl's $230M raised total. The streaming capability is a product segment within Hudl's broader sports analytics platform.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Hudl TV serves sports streaming to programs using Hudl's platform. KTV serves every KaNeXT mode (Business, Education, Community, Athletics, Personal) as a general streaming infrastructure with intelligence and commerce integration.

### Twitch / YouTube Live (Streaming Infrastructure)

Twitch was acquired by Amazon for $970M in 2014. YouTube is part of Alphabet ($2T+ market cap). These are consumer streaming platforms at scale.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Consumer streaming platforms serving millions of creators and viewers. KTV is vertical streaming infrastructure integrated into institutional operations. Different use case, structurally different deployment model.

### Live Streaming Platform Layer Summary

Streaming infrastructure investment at sports-program-streaming scale is in the hundreds of millions to low billions across the category. KTV is the streaming layer of a broader platform; valuing it standalone understates its integration value.

---

## Layer 5: Payments and Fintech (KPay)

KaNeXT KPay scope: wallet, payments, settlement, commerce processing, remittance, deposit infrastructure, planned bank charter integration.

### Stripe

Stripe provides online payment processing infrastructure for businesses globally.

**Private company:** Valued at $159B in February 2026 tender offer (up from $107B in 2025). Total payment volume processed in 2025: $1.9 trillion. 2024 revenue: $5.11B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Stripe is the dominant payments infrastructure for internet-scale businesses. KPay is embedded payments infrastructure inside KaNeXT platform, integrated with wallet, commerce, streaming, and institutional operations. Different deployment model (platform-embedded vs API-first developer platform).

### Adyen

Adyen provides a global payment platform serving enterprise merchants.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $35-50B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Enterprise payment processing. Similar category to Stripe; different deployment.

### Block (Square)

Block provides small business payment processing, Cash App consumer wallet, and lending.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $45-50B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Combines merchant payments with consumer wallet, comparable to some KPay capabilities. Consumer wallet and merchant processing are two components; KPay extends into institutional deployment, remittance, and commerce processing across a platform.

### Remitly

Remitly provides digital cross-border remittance services to immigrants and their families globally.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $3.6-4B (April 2026). TTM revenue $1.64B. Growing revenue 19-20% annually.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Remitly is the remittance specialist comparable. KPay includes remittance capability as one of its functions alongside commerce processing, wallet, and institutional deposits. Remitly at $3.6-4B market cap for remittance alone establishes the value scale for cross-border payment specialization.

### Chime, Current (Consumer Digital Banking)

Chime valued at approximately $25B in secondary markets. Current valued at approximately $2-5B.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Consumer digital banking products. KPay's consumer wallet functionality overlaps; KPay extends into institutional treasury, commerce, and platform integration that consumer neobanks do not.

### Payments and Fintech Layer Summary

| Company | Valuation | Scope |
|---|---|---|
| Stripe | $159B private (2026) | Online payments infrastructure |
| Adyen | ~$35-50B market cap | Enterprise payments |
| Block | ~$45-50B market cap | Merchant + consumer wallet |
| Remitly | ~$3.6-4B market cap | Digital remittance |
| Chime | ~$25B secondary | Consumer neobank |

Aggregate payments and fintech layer market cap: $270-290B+ across the category. KPay is the payments and fintech layer of a platform that integrates payments with streaming, commerce, institutional operations, and intelligence.

---

## Layer 6: Real-Time Stats Platform (KStat)

KaNeXT KStat scope: real-time stats and scorekeeping across 14 sport specifications covering 26 sport configurations (basketball, soccer, flag football, volleyball, hockey, lacrosse, golf, tennis, track, cheer, swim, football, baseball, wrestling, boxing) with live scoring, box scores, play-by-play, and statistical intelligence integration.

### GameChanger (by Dick's Sporting Goods)

GameChanger provides real-time stats and livestreaming for youth sports. Acquired by DICK'S Sporting Goods.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Youth-sports focused stats. KStat covers amateur through professional competitive levels with architectural depth.

### MaxPreps (subset of CBS Sports)

MaxPreps provides high school sports stats and scores. Part of CBS Sports.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** High school sports stats aggregation. KStat covers collegiate and professional as well.

### Real-Time Stats Platform Layer Summary

Real-time stats platforms primarily exist as segments within larger sports media and analytics companies (GameChanger within Dick's, MaxPreps within CBS). Standalone stats platforms sell to teams and leagues at $50-200M acquisition ranges. KStat extends real-time stats across 14 sport specifications with intelligence integration.

---

## Layer 7: Video Intelligence (KVision)

KaNeXT KVision scope: in-house video intelligence pipeline, camera-to-structured-data processing, video analysis integrated with intelligence reasoning.

### Hudl (Video Intelligence subset)

Hudl's core product is sports video intelligence. Already included in Layer 1 above.

### Veritone

Veritone provides AI-powered video intelligence platform for enterprise applications.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $50-200M depending on period.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Enterprise AI video processing. KVision applies video intelligence inside sports-specific architecture.

### Video Intelligence Layer Summary

The video intelligence category is primarily embedded inside sports analytics companies (Hudl) or enterprise AI companies. Standalone video intelligence platforms are in the hundreds of millions valuation range.

---

## Layer 8: Gaming Platform (KPlay)

KaNeXT KPlay scope: gaming, simulation, educational games built on intelligence architecture.

### Zwift

Zwift provides indoor cycling training with virtual racing and community features.

**Private company:** Valued at approximately $1B+ in recent rounds.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Fitness gaming. KPlay applies sports intelligence to gaming experiences across the multi-sport database.

### Peloton

Peloton provides connected fitness gaming with instructor-led content.

**Public company:** Market capitalization approximately $1-3B depending on period.

**Scope vs KaNeXT:** Connected fitness hardware and content. KPlay is software-based sports gaming built on intelligence foundation.

### Gaming Platform Layer Summary

Sports and fitness gaming platforms span $1-15B in valuations across the category. KPlay is the gaming expression of KaNeXT's intelligence architecture, leveraging the underlying 250K+ athlete database and 27+ sport simulation capability.

---

## Layer 9: Hardware and Sensors (Smart Ball, Cameras)

KaNeXT hardware scope: Smart Ball sensor architecture across 9 ball sports (basketball, football, soccer, volleyball, baseball, softball, tennis, handball, futsal) plus camera architecture for KVision deployment.

### Catapult Sports (covered in Layer 1)

Wearables and sensor-based performance analytics. $684M market cap.

### Whoop

Whoop provides wearable fitness and recovery tracking. Private company valued at approximately $3.6B.

### Wilson Sporting Goods Labs

Wilson (parent to major ball manufacturers) has been developing sensor-embedded balls. Wilson is a subsidiary of Amer Sports (public company, market cap approximately $10-15B).

### Hardware and Sensors Layer Summary

Sensor hardware for sports spans from wearables to embedded ball sensors. Individual companies in the space range from $500M to $15B depending on breadth. Smart Ball integrated across 9 ball sports with unified intelligence is architecturally deeper than any single-sport sensor product on the market.

---

## Layer 10: The Integration Premium

This layer does not map to a single comparable company. It maps to the question: what does it cost to integrate all of the above into one governed architecture?

### Salesforce as Integration Case Study

Salesforce has acquired more than 70 companies and invested tens of billions of dollars in integration over two decades. The Customer 360 initiative remains incomplete by Salesforce's own reporting. Multi-cloud integration is the largest persistent investment category at Salesforce.

### Microsoft as Integration Case Study

Microsoft's M365 and Azure platforms integrate Office, Teams, SharePoint, Dynamics, LinkedIn, and GitHub. Each acquisition cost billions. Integration across the M365 stack is a decade-long ongoing investment.

### The KaNeXT Integration Reality

KaNeXT integrated 10 product layers in one governed architecture built by one founder. The universal RBAC spans all 5 modes. Data flows through Dipson across every tile in every mode. The intelligence is called the same way from an admissions query as from a basketball scouting report. The payment processed at a volleyball game flows through the same wallet that handled tuition.

Companies that attempt this integration through acquisition fail more often than they succeed. The companies in the layers above rarely merge well. Hudl acquires StatsBomb, Balltime, FastModel, and Titan Sports. Teamworks acquires INFLCR, ARMS, Smartabase, Zelus, Telemetry, Basepath. Both companies then spend years integrating acquired products into unified workflows. The acquisition model creates product sprawl; the unified architecture model (KaNeXT) creates coherence.

The integration premium is not a number. It is the architectural coherence that companies attempting acquisition-driven integration struggle to achieve at any price.

---

## Cross-Layer Summary

Aggregate market value across publicly traded and privately valued companies covering portions of KaNeXT's scope:

**Sports Intelligence Layer:** ~$10-15B (Hudl, Sportradar, Genius Sports, Catapult, Stats Perform, Teamworks combined)

**Institutional Operating Systems Layer:** ~$290B+ (Workday, PowerSchool, Ellucian, Salesforce portions attributable to institutional operations, Microsoft 365 portions)

**AI Intelligence Infrastructure Layer:** ~$450-475B+ (Palantir, Databricks, Snowflake)

**Payments and Fintech Layer:** ~$270-290B+ (Stripe, Adyen, Block, Remitly, Chime)

**Streaming, Video Intelligence, Stats, Gaming, Hardware Layers:** ~$15-30B combined across the fragmented comparables

The aggregate market capitalization across the categories KaNeXT spans approaches or exceeds $1 trillion across publicly traded and privately valued companies, each covering portions of what KaNeXT has built in a single integrated architecture.

KaNeXT does not claim a $1 trillion replacement cost. KaNeXT demonstrates architectural breadth across layers whose aggregate market value is in that range. The replication challenge is not one company's worth of R&D. The replication challenge is coordinating investment and integration across a portfolio of acquisition targets that no company has successfully combined.

---

## What This Means For The Year 1 Capital Raise

The Year 1 $33M capital raise is positioned against an intelligence IP and integrated platform whose components individually map to companies valued in the billions to hundreds of billions. The architectural coherence across layers is itself the most distinctive asset. The Year 1 raise is a fraction of a percent of the aggregate comparable-company valuations across the categories KaNeXT spans.

The market context is clear. The replication cost question answers itself when the full comparable landscape is examined.

---

## Disclaimer

All valuations and market capitalizations referenced are from public filings and reporting as of April 2026 where available. Private company valuations reflect most recent published funding rounds or secondary market activity. Acquisition valuations reflect announced transaction values. Market valuations change materially over time; this document provides a point-in-time comparison. The scope comparisons between KaNeXT and comparable companies are based on published product descriptions and do not imply equivalence in scale, revenue, customer base, or operational maturity. KaNeXT is commercially early while the comparables are commercially mature. The comparison addresses architectural scope, not current operating scale.

# Comparable Companies Analysis

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## Purpose

This document presents the market context for KaNeXT's intelligence architecture. The landscape of sports intelligence, institutional software, and adjacent categories is highly fragmented. Different companies solve different parts of what KaNeXT has built in a single integrated architecture. This document presents the public and private valuations of those companies, what each covers, and lets the reader evaluate KaNeXT's scope in that context.

KaNeXT does not claim a specific replacement cost or enterprise value in this document. It presents the market data and lets the reader evaluate what one integrated intelligence operating system across 50+ domains, 27+ sports, institutional functions, league governance, NIL, market intelligence, and hardware is worth relative to a landscape where these capabilities exist as separate companies each valued in the hundreds of millions to billions of dollars.

All valuation data cited reflects publicly reported figures as of research date April 2026.

---

## Category 1: Governed Intelligence Operating Systems

Companies that build governed intelligence infrastructure that institutions depend on operationally. Closest structural parallel to what KaNeXT has built across institutional and sport intelligence.

### Palantir Technologies (NASDAQ: PLTR)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$350B (April 2026)
- **Revenue (TTM):** $4.47B
- **Cumulative R&D since 2003 founding:** $4.5-6B estimated
- **Employees:** ~4,430
- **Coverage:** Government intelligence (55% of revenue), commercial enterprise intelligence (45%). Platforms: Gotham (government), Foundry (enterprise), Apollo (deployment), AIP (AI platform).
- **Scope limitation:** Government and commercial enterprise intelligence only. Does not cover sports, education institutional operations, athletics, or consumer-facing applications.

### Databricks
- **Valuation:** ~$62B (private)
- **Coverage:** Data lakehouse and AI platform for enterprise data engineering and analytics. Foundational data infrastructure layer.
- **Scope limitation:** Infrastructure platform; not a vertical intelligence system for any specific industry.

### Snowflake (NYSE: SNOW)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$60B
- **Coverage:** Cloud data warehousing and analytics platform for enterprises.
- **Scope limitation:** Horizontal data infrastructure; not a vertical intelligence operating system.

---

## Category 2: Sports Intelligence and Analytics

Companies focused on sports data, analytics, video, and performance intelligence. The most fragmented competitive landscape in the KaNeXT scope.

### Hudl (Private)
- **Revenue:** $730M+ (2024)
- **Customers:** 325,000+ teams globally
- **Employees:** 3,500
- **Total raised:** $230M across six rounds; valuation undisclosed as private. Founded 2006. Major investor: Bain Capital Tech Opportunities.
- **Coverage:** Video analysis, smart camera hardware, livestreaming, recruiting support, performance analytics across 30+ sports. Recent acquisitions include StatsBomb (2024), BlueFrame, Titan Sports (2025), FastModel (2025), Balltime (2025).
- **Scope limitation:** Video-centric workflow. Does not include institutional operations, league governance, NIL management, market intelligence, or comprehensive evaluation architecture across the full sport-athletic-institutional stack.

### Sportradar Group (NASDAQ: SRAD)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$4.5-5B (April 2026)
- **Revenue (TTM):** $1.45B
- **Coverage:** Sports betting data, media data services, official league data partnerships (Premier League, La Liga, WTA, FIBA). Integrity services, iGaming content.
- **Scope limitation:** Betting and data distribution focused. Acquired Synergy Sports for basketball analytics. Does not cover institutional intelligence, athlete development evaluation, recruiting intelligence at program level, or academic-institutional integration.

### Stats Perform (Private, Vista Equity Partners)
- **Total raised:** $745M
- **Coverage:** Sports data collection (500,000+ matches, 3,900 competitions annually), AI/ML predictive models. Owns Opta brand. Clients: ESPN, Google, Bet365, William Hill, FIBA, La Liga, WTA, Serie A, Premier League.
- **Employees:** 3,270
- **Scope limitation:** Sports data and predictive analytics focused. Does not cover institutional operations, NIL intelligence, athlete life-cycle development, or cross-institutional deployment.

### Genius Sports (NYSE: GENI)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$2-3B
- **Coverage:** Sports data, betting technology, fan engagement. Went public via $1.5B SPAC merger (2021). Acquired Second Spectrum (spatial sports tracking) for approximately $200M.
- **Scope limitation:** Betting, broadcasting, and fan engagement focused. Does not cover institutional operations or comprehensive evaluation architecture.

### Catapult Sports (ASX: CAT)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$500M-$1B (Australian publicly traded)
- **Coverage:** Wearable performance monitoring hardware, GPS tracking, biomechanics. Elite and professional sports focus.
- **Scope limitation:** Sensor hardware and physical performance tracking. Does not include video analysis, evaluation systems, recruiting, or institutional operations.

### Synergy Sports (Now part of Sportradar)
- **Acquired for:** ~$100M estimated (2022)
- **Coverage:** Basketball video and analytics; expanded to baseball, softball, volleyball. Professional league partnerships.
- **Scope limitation:** Video-centric analytics across limited sport portfolio. Does not cover player evaluation modeling, institutional operations, league governance, or broader intelligence architecture.

---

## Category 3: Institutional Education Software

Companies that build enterprise software for higher education institutions. Structural parallel to KaNeXT's institutional operating system layer.

### Ellucian (Private, Blackstone + Vista Equity Partners)
- **Acquisition valuation:** $5B+ (June 2021 Blackstone/Vista purchase)
- **Previous acquisition:** $3.5B (2015 TPG/Leonard Green purchase)
- **Coverage:** Higher education ERP and SIS. Serves 2,800+ institutions across 50 countries, 20M+ students. Acquired Anthology's SIS/ERP business December 2025 after Anthology's Chapter 11 bankruptcy, adding 260+ institutions.
- **Scope limitation:** Administrative ERP and SIS. Does not cover athletics, intelligence, evaluation, media, communications, or consumer-facing platform functions.

### Anthology (Filed Chapter 11, 2025)
- **Outcome:** Bankruptcy reorganization; SIS/ERP business sold to Ellucian December 2025
- **Prior scope:** Higher education ERP, SIS, and learning management (Blackboard). Serves 150M+ users prior to reorganization.
- **Scope limitation:** Administrative education software. Financial distress illustrates that even category leaders at significant scale face existential risk under fragmented vendor models.

### Workday (NASDAQ: WDAY)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$65-70B
- **Coverage:** Enterprise HR, finance, and planning. Expanding into higher education administration.
- **Scope limitation:** Horizontal enterprise software adapted for higher education; not purpose-built for the integrated academic-athletic-institutional-community model.

### Handshake (Private)
- **Latest valuation:** $3.5B
- **Coverage:** Career services, student-employer matching, campus recruiting.
- **Scope limitation:** Career services niche only. Does not cover athletics, evaluation, academic operations, or broader institutional functions.

---

## Category 4: Athlete Management and NIL Intelligence

Companies serving the athlete monetization and representation layer. New category emerged post-NCAA NIL policy change (July 2021). Total NIL market projected to reach $2.5B+ annually.

### Teamworks / INFLCR (Private)
- **Scope:** Teamworks is the athlete management platform; acquired INFLCR (NIL content management) in 2019. Appointed by NCAA as the third-party administrator for the NIL registry (2024).
- **Valuation:** Estimated $500M+ range based on venture funding and NCAA registry selection.
- **Coverage:** Athlete content, communication, NIL compliance tracking, athlete life cycle operations. Serves professional sports, collegiate athletics, Olympic/National Governing Bodies, military/tactical organizations.
- **Scope limitation:** Operations and compliance focused. Does not include evaluation intelligence, recruiting analytics at program depth, institutional integration beyond athletics operations, or cross-sport intelligence architecture.

### Opendorse (Private)
- **Latest raise:** $20M Series B (2024)
- **Coverage:** NIL marketplace, compliance, fair market value assessment, brand deal facilitation. Serves 100,000+ college athletes, $250M+ transactions processed since 2021.
- **Scope limitation:** NIL marketplace only. Does not cover athletic intelligence, recruiting evaluation, institutional operations, or coaching tools.

### Learfield (Private, private equity-backed)
- **Coverage:** Collegiate multimedia rights, sponsorships, and NIL. Operates CLC brand (trademark licensing for colleges).
- **Valuation:** $1B+ estimated. Private equity portfolio company.
- **Scope limitation:** Multimedia rights and sponsorship management. Does not include evaluation, recruiting intelligence, or institutional operations.

### Altius Sports Partners (Private)
- **Coverage:** NIL strategy, collective development, compliance advisory.
- **Scope limitation:** Consulting and advisory services; not an intelligence platform.

---

## Category 5: League Governance and Compliance Infrastructure

Software that automates compliance and governance for athletic associations. Smaller market, less mature.

### ARMS (Athletic Recruiting Management Software)
- **Coverage:** Recruiting compliance tracking, eligibility monitoring for NCAA athletic departments.
- **Scope limitation:** Compliance-specific workflow tool. Does not include evaluation, intelligence, or broader institutional integration.

### Teamworks (referenced above)
- **NCAA NIL Registry administrator** role establishes Teamworks as infrastructure-level provider for the association.

---

## Category 6: Hardware and Sensor Intelligence

Companies building sensor hardware that generates sport performance data. Fragmented category with limited integration into broader intelligence systems.

### Catapult Sports (referenced above)
- Wearables focus. $500M-$1B market cap range.

### ShotTracker (Private)
- **Coverage:** Basketball sensor hardware for shot tracking, player tracking.
- **Scope limitation:** Single-sport sensor product.

### Zebra Technologies (NASDAQ: ZBRA)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$12B
- **Coverage:** RFID and tracking infrastructure; NFL Next Gen Stats partnership.
- **Scope limitation:** Hardware tracking infrastructure; not a vertical sports intelligence product.

---

## Category 7: Betting and Market Intelligence

Sports betting data, odds, and market intelligence. Major public-market category.

### Sportradar (referenced above)
- Dual classification: sports analytics and betting intelligence. $4.5-5B market cap.

### Genius Sports (referenced above)
- Dual classification: sports analytics and betting. $2-3B market cap.

### Kambi Group (Stockholm: KAMBI)
- **Market capitalization:** ~$300-500M
- **Coverage:** Sports betting platform services.

---

## The Market Context Summary

The intelligence landscape across sports, institutional operations, athlete management, and market intelligence is fragmented across dozens of companies, each solving a narrow slice of what KaNeXT has built as a single integrated architecture:

| Category | Representative Companies | Valuation Range | What KaNeXT Covers in Category |
|---|---|---|---|
| Governed Intelligence OS | Palantir | $350B public | Institutional intelligence: 27 modules across People and Talent, Operations and Infrastructure, Leadership and Governance, Growth and External, Finance and Assets |
| Sports Intelligence (broad) | Hudl, Sportradar, Stats Perform | $700M-$5B each | All 27+ sport domains covered with evaluation depth beyond video-only competitors |
| Sports Intelligence (depth) | Synergy, Second Spectrum, Hudl acquisitions | $100-500M each | Full evaluation architecture across every sport, not video-only |
| Institutional Education Software | Ellucian, Workday, Handshake | $3.5B-$70B each | KaNeXT OS covers institutional operations within an integrated platform |
| NIL and Athlete Management | Teamworks, Opendorse, Learfield | $500M-$1B each | NIL intelligence integrated with recruiting, evaluation, and institutional systems |
| Hardware/Sensor | Catapult, Zebra, ShotTracker | $500M-$12B | Smart Ball architecture across 9 sports integrated with intelligence system |
| Betting and Market Intelligence | Sportradar, Genius Sports, Kambi | $300M-$5B each | Market intelligence integrated with sport and league governance architecture |
| Governance and Compliance | ARMS, Teamworks compliance, NIL registry | $100M-$500M each | League governance protocols and compliance intelligence integrated with platform |

**Total addressable market segments represented above: approximately $420B in combined market capitalization across publicly traded comparables, plus additional billions in private-market comparables.** This figure includes a single Palantir data point ($350B) that alone exceeds every other comparable combined. Excluding Palantir (which covers government/enterprise intelligence beyond KaNeXT's current scope), the remaining sports, institutional, NIL, hardware, compliance, and betting infrastructure comparables aggregate to approximately $70-80B in publicly traded market value plus tens of billions more in private market value.

---

## What Makes KaNeXT Structurally Different

Each of the comparables above solves one component of the operational need. KaNeXT solves them as one architecture.

**No existing company combines:**
- 27+ sport domains at evaluation depth (beyond Hudl's video, beyond Synergy's basketball-only, beyond Stats Perform's data)
- Institutional operations intelligence (comparable to the scope Palantir covers in government/enterprise, applied to education institutions)
- League governance across NCAA D1/D2/D3, NAIA, NJCAA, USCAA, NCCAA, professional leagues worldwide
- NIL intelligence integrated with recruiting and compliance
- Market intelligence for betting and gaming integration
- Hardware intelligence across 9 ball sports (Smart Ball)
- Media infrastructure (KTV), financial infrastructure (KPay), communication infrastructure (VoIP)
- Consumer-facing platform (institutions, families, athletes, fans, communities) built on the same architecture

Every comparable above is a partial solution requiring integration with other partial solutions. Institutions currently buy Hudl plus Ellucian plus Teamworks plus separate enrollment software plus separate commerce plus separate video plus separate compliance plus separate recruiting plus separate media. Each integration point is a cost, a failure point, and an architectural compromise.

KaNeXT is the first platform building the integrated alternative. The operational thesis is that the integration premium (reduced vendor fragmentation, unified data architecture, governed intelligence across all domains) produces value that exceeds the sum of the components.

---

## Reading This Document for Valuation Context

This document does not propose a specific valuation for KaNeXT. It presents the market data and the scope mapping. Different investors will draw different conclusions depending on:

- What weight they give to replacement cost as a valuation anchor
- What multiples they apply to KaNeXT's projected revenue relative to the comparable companies' multiples
- How they discount for execution risk at KaNeXT's pre-commercial-scale stage
- How they weight the integrated-architecture premium versus the proven-revenue premium comparable companies have earned

The Valuation Framework document provides multiple lenses for applying these considerations. This document provides the market context those lenses reference.

---

All valuation and financial data cited reflects publicly reported figures as of April 2026. Private company valuations are estimates based on publicly reported funding rounds, acquisition prices, and industry estimates where available. Market capitalizations for publicly traded companies fluctuate daily. Acquisition prices cited may not reflect all terms of a transaction. This document presents market data for context; it does not constitute investment advice, an offer, or a solicitation. Independent financial due diligence should supplement the information provided here.

# Investor Economics Summary

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

This document summarizes the Year 1 capital raise and the economics of participation. It is an investor-facing orientation document, not a legal term sheet. Specific legal terms, subscription agreements, and definitive documents are provided to qualified investors after initial diligence conversations. Final terms are subject to securities counsel review.

---

## The Raise

**$33M total across two parallel instruments.**

| Instrument | Size | Structure | Dilution |
|---|---|---|---|
| KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC | $30M | 1.5x fixed return | Zero equity |
| Parallel SAFE | $3M | $100M valuation cap | ~3% at cap |
| **Combined** | **$33M** | | |

Capital deployment is gated on execution of the Athletics-Only Agreement with South Florida Bible College & Theological Seminary (SFBC). Capital does not flow before partnership execution.

---

## Three Investor Classes

### Class 1: Fund LP ($30M target, 1.5x fixed return)

Participation in KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC.

- **What you put in:** Minimum investment set at the subscription agreement stage
- **What you get back:** 1.5x your capital as a fixed return obligation
- **Example:** $1M in returns $1.5M. $5M in returns $7.5M. $10M in returns $15M.
- **Equity:** None. This is a fixed-return structure, not an equity position.
- **Timeline:** Return obligation over the fund's stated term
- **Risk posture:** Structured return, not variable equity upside. Investor receives the 1.5x regardless of company outcome above or below that threshold, subject to the fund's ability to pay.

### Class 2: SAFE Participant ($3M total, $100M cap)

Parallel friends and family round. Designed for individual accredited investors at smaller check sizes than the fund.

- **What you put in:** SAFE investment amount of your choice
- **What you get:** Conversion to equity at the next priced round at the lower of: (a) the next round's pre-money valuation, or (b) the $100M cap
- **Example at $100M cap:** $100K in = approximately 0.1% equity at conversion. $500K in = approximately 0.5% equity at conversion.
- **Total SAFE dilution to founder:** Approximately 3% at the $100M cap, across all SAFE participants combined
- **Timeline:** Converts at the next priced round
- **Risk posture:** Equity exposure with cap protection. If company scales, SAFE participants get meaningful upside through equity conversion.

### Class 3: Strategic Equity Partner (selective, negotiated)

Reserved for a small number of strategic partners whose participation brings distribution, credibility, or operational value beyond capital. Equity range 5-20%, negotiated individually.

- **Who this is for:** Named media, operational, and distribution partners bringing specific strategic value
- **What you put in:** Capital plus strategic contribution (distribution, advisory, credibility)
- **What you get:** Negotiated equity position
- **Timeline:** Negotiated at time of transaction
- **Access:** By invitation only. Not an open category.

---

## What The Capital Funds

Year 1 deployment breakdown:

| Category | Amount |
|---|---|
| Athletics (6 Varsity sports, 12 teams) | $13.5M |
| Housing and Feeding | $4.0M |
| KaNeXT Core Operations | $6.4M |
| Partner Institution Support | $2.1M |
| Buffer and Reserve | $4.0M |
| **Total** | **$30.0M** |

The $3M SAFE adds working capital and buffer. Full breakdown is in Capital Deployment document.

---

## What Protects The Capital

Year 1 is asset-light by design. The Year 1 capital is protected by:

- **Intelligence IP.** 50+ intelligence domains, 400+ files, 250,000+ athlete database. Replacement cost across the 10 product layers KaNeXT spans is substantial. See Platform Replication Landscape.
- **Live operational product.** TestFlight deployment with operational OS, Dipson AI, intelligence engines, KTV, KPay running today. Not a prototype.
- **Partnership structure.** Athletics-Only Agreement with a real ABHE-accredited institution with existing operations, enrollment, and revenue.
- **Capital gating.** Capital does not deploy until partnership is executed. No partnership, no deployment.

Miami Lakes campus acquisition and bank charter are Year 2+ capital events raised separately. Year 1 is not secured against future real estate or banking assets.

---

## Diligence and Next Steps

Interested investors typically proceed as follows.

1. **Review the data room** to understand the thesis, product, institutional strategy, and growth model.
2. **Schedule a founder conversation** to walk through the app, see Dipson live, and discuss alignment.
3. **Request investor-specific documentation** appropriate to your class (subscription agreement for Fund LP, SAFE agreement for SAFE participants, individually negotiated terms for Strategic Equity).
4. **Counsel review and execution** on both sides.

All subscription and SAFE documentation is provided after initial diligence conversations, subject to accreditation verification and counsel review.

Specific terms, risk factors, and legal disclosures are provided in the definitive subscription agreements reviewed by securities counsel. # KaNeXT LLC - Ownership and Governance Summary

## OWNERSHIP STRUCTURE

This structure is designed to preserve clear founder ownership, segregate intellectual property from operations, and distinguish fund LP interests from operating-company equity.

Oluwadara Samuel Kalejaiye (Sammy Kalejaiye) owns 100% of OSK Group LLC, a Florida holding company. OSK Group LLC owns 100% of all operating subsidiaries:

- **KaNeXT LLC** (FL) - Operating company. General Partner of KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC.
- **KaNeXT IP LLC** (FL) - Holds all intellectual property, including the intelligence system, KaNeXT OS architecture, all canonical specifications, and trademarks. KaNeXT LLC operates under license from KaNeXT IP LLC.
- **KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC** (FL) - Fund entity. GP is KaNeXT LLC.

No equity in any entity has been issued or transferred to any party other than the founder as of the date of this document.

---

## FUND INVESTORS - OWNERSHIP POSITION

Investors in KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC hold LP interests in the fund entity only. Fund investors own 0% of OSK Group LLC, KaNeXT LLC, KaNeXT IP LLC, or any affiliated entity. LP interests do not convert to equity in any operating or holding entity under any circumstances.

Fund investors have no board seats, no voting rights, no governance rights, and no conversion mechanism with respect to any entity in the corporate structure.

---

## GOVERNANCE

All entities are governed solely by their equity holders. As of the date of this document, that is Oluwadara Samuel Kalejaiye exclusively, through OSK Group LLC.

No outside board seats exist. No advisory board holds governance authority. No investor, whether through a fund, infrastructure vehicle, or otherwise, holds any right to appoint directors, approve decisions, veto actions, or participate in operational or strategic decision-making.

This reflects the current governance structure as of the date of this document and does not preclude future board formation, equity grants, or governance changes at the founder's discretion.

# KaNeXT Capital Deployment

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## Overview

The Year 1 capital raise funds the Year 1 partnership launch. Total target is $33M across two parallel instruments: a $30M fund and a $3M SAFE. Capital deploys upon partnership execution with the partner institution (South Florida Bible College & Theological Seminary, a forty-year-old ABHE-accredited evangelical Christian institution), against the Year 1 operating scope defined in the Athletics Operating Agreement and supporting documents.

The Year 1 capital is a concentrated bet on one transformation. It does not fund campus acquisition, bank charter, platform infrastructure buildout, or mandate rollout. Those are future capital events raised separately against proven execution at the partner institution. This capital funds the partnership launch, the athletic program buildout, platform deployment, operational infrastructure, and Year 1 buffer.

---

## Capital Structure

**$30M Fund (KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC).** Structured for a 1.5x return to limited partners, total return obligation of $45M, with zero equity dilution to the KaNeXT operating entity or founder. The fund is the primary capital vehicle. Limited partners receive a fixed return structure rather than equity participation, preserving the operating company's capitalization structure and the founder's ownership.

**$3M Parallel SAFE.** Friends & Family round sized at $3M with a $100M valuation cap. Approximately 3% dilution at the cap. Converts to equity at the next priced round. Structured parallel to the fund, not as a replacement, targeting individual accredited investors with ticket sizes typical for F&F participation.

**Combined total: $33M.** The fund provides the primary deployment capital. The SAFE adds working capital and buffer while expanding the relational network of individual investors participating in the raise.

Full fund mechanics, SAFE conversion terms, and investor economics are detailed in the term sheet document.

---

## Year 1 Deployment Breakdown

The $30M deployment covers the operational scope for Year 1 partnership launch at the partner institution.

| Category | Amount |
|---|---|
| Athletics | $13.5M |
| Housing + Feeding | $4.0M |
| KaNeXT Core Operations | $6.4M |
| Partner Institution Support | $2.1M |
| Buffer / Reserve | $4.0M |
| **Total** | **$30.0M** |

### Athletics ($13.5M)

Full operational funding for six Varsity programs with two teams per sport (Varsity plus Development = 12 teams) in Year 1. Year 1 scholarship structure is strategic: minimal scholarships deployed only where recruiting requires it, with strategic budget reserved for exceptional situations. Most athletes receive Title IV federal financial aid plus standard institutional aid. NAIA Varsity scholarship equivalencies activate in Year 2 upon NAIA membership approval. NIL distribution through KPay operates from Day 1. Championship-caliber coaching staffs funded above NAIA market rates. Full athletic training and medical support. Weight room and training facility equipment and buildout. Athletic facility access through commercial gym partnerships and junior college arrangements. Game operations, travel, equipment, recruiting, and athletic department administration. Capital reserved from strategic scholarship savings deploys to premium program quality across coaching compensation, facilities, recruiting infrastructure, and NIL reserves.

### Housing + Feeding ($4.0M)

Master-leased cluster housing in the South Florida market proximate to athletic facility partners. Housing infrastructure for all Varsity scholarship athletes and development tier athletes electing cluster housing. Team rooms, study space, residence life support, nutrition integration. Team dining infrastructure through contracted food service operations.

### KaNeXT Core Operations ($6.4M)

Founder and team compensation and benefits. Corporate infrastructure: office, legal, accounting, insurance, technology. Platform operations: server and infrastructure costs for KaNeXT OS, Dipson, KTV, KPay, KStat, KVision, and supporting systems. Ongoing engineering and platform development. Intellectual property protection. Corporate governance and compliance. Investment in institutional quality at the partner institution, including faculty compensation uplift above the Christian university market, academic program development, student services excellence, and academic infrastructure that supports the tuition trajectory described in the institutional revenue model.

### Partner Institution Support ($2.1M)

Direct financial support to the partner institution through the partnership structure. Operational Partnership Fee paid annually. Philanthropic Contribution to the institution. Institutional integration infrastructure. Compliance and coordination costs associated with the Athletics Operating Agreement.

### Buffer / Reserve ($4.0M)

Working capital and contingency reserve. Protects against unforeseen capital needs, timing mismatches between expenses and revenue, and operational variance in the first year of a new partnership. The buffer is standard prudence at this scale and stage.

---

## Deployment Principles

**Partnership-gated.** Capital deployment is gated on execution of the Athletics Operating Agreement with SFBC. The raise and the partnership are sequenced, not simultaneous. Capital does not flow before partnership execution.

**Asset-light Year 1.** No campus acquisition, no facility construction, no hardware manufacturing, no bank charter. Facilities are accessed through leasing and partnerships. Housing is master-leased. The platform operates on existing cloud infrastructure. Year 1 is an operational deployment, not an infrastructure build.

**Concentrated, not diversified.** The capital funds one partnership at one institution. No parallel deployments at other institutions. No speculative allocations to future opportunities. Every dollar supports the partner institution transformation.

**Software-first.** Platform deployment at the partner institution and at GAAC operates on the existing KaNeXT OS, which is live and operational. The software is the product. Hardware and infrastructure buildouts (cameras, fulfillment, VoIP telephony infrastructure, bank operations) are future capital events not required for Year 1 success.

**Buffer-preserved.** The $4M buffer exists because first-year operations at new partnerships always encounter variance. The buffer is not padding. It is working capital that makes Year 1 survivable through the normal turbulence of launch.

---

## Year 1 Sources and Uses Reconciliation

The $30M fund deployment categories above map onto the detailed Year 1 operating expense categories in the Operating Budget and Expense Model through a sources-and-uses framework that includes the SAFE and first-year revenue.

**Year 1 Sources of Capital:**

| Source | Amount |
|---|---|
| Fund (KaNeXT Capital Fund I LLC) | $30.0M |
| SAFE ($100M cap) | $3.0M |
| Year 1 operational revenue (midpoint) | ~$1.75M |
| **Total Year 1 capital sources** | **~$34.75M** |

**Year 1 Uses of Capital:**

| Use | Amount |
|---|---|
| Operating expenses (per Operating Budget: athletics $13.5M + enrollment $3.5M + tech/platform $5.8M + campus ops $4.0M + corporate/admin $4.0M + online $0.8M) | $31.6M |
| Partner Institution Support (operational partnership fee + philanthropic contribution) | $2.1M |
| **Total Year 1 capital uses** | **$33.7M** |

**Balance:** Year 1 sources ($34.75M) exceed uses ($33.7M) by approximately $1M, providing a small operational cushion in addition to the $4M buffer held in reserve. The buffer is accounted for in the $30M fund deployment above ("Buffer / Reserve") but is not consumed by operating expenses unless variance events require it.

The capital deployment categories in this document (Athletics, Housing + Feeding, Core Ops, Partner Support, Buffer) are the strategic framing. The operating budget categories (Athletic Operations, Enrollment and Marketing, Technology and Platform, Campus Operations, Corporate and Administrative, Online Program Delivery) are the operational accounting. Both views describe the same $30M fund plus the $3M SAFE. The Operating Budget and Expense Model document shows the line-item detail by operational category.

---

## Forward Capital Architecture

The Year 1 raise is the first deployment in a multi-stage capital plan. Subsequent capital is raised against proven execution at the partner institution. Each future capital event is scoped, structured, and priced at the time of deployment based on operational results and market conditions.

**Campus Acquisition Capital.** Miami Lakes campus land acquisition and early development. Activates when the partner institution reaches the fully-built state described in the institutional strategy documents.

**Platform Infrastructure Capital.** Camera company acquisition, fulfillment center operations, VoIP telecommunications infrastructure. Activates as mandate deployment scales demand for hardware and operational support.

**Bank Charter Capital.** Community bank acquisition and Minority Depository Institution capitalization. Activates when deposit volume from platform commerce justifies the charter.

**Mandate Rollout Capital.** Governing body mandate deployment across NAIA, NJCAA, USCAA, and NCCAA. Activates after GAAC proves the model.

Each capital event is concentrated on a specific milestone, not speculative buildout. The Year 1 raise is the foundation that earns KaNeXT the right to raise the subsequent capital. No commitments, timelines, or valuations for future raises are implied in the Year 1 capital documents.

---

## Founder Economics

**Year 1 founder cash compensation: $85,000.**

This is the salary figure for the Year 1 budget. The founder retains 100% equity ownership of OSK Group LLC, which owns KaNeXT LLC and all subsidiaries. The low cash compensation reflects founder alignment with investor outcomes: the returns are in the execution, not in short-term salary.

Standard corporate infrastructure (benefits, business expenses, technology, travel) is handled through ordinary operating expenses within the $6.4M Core Operations line. The salary figure represents direct cash compensation to the founder as an employee of the operating entity.

---

## Disclaimer

All capital deployment figures are estimates based on Year 1 operational planning. Actual deployment amounts may vary within each category based on execution, opportunity cost considerations, and operational conditions. The raise amount, fund structure, and SAFE terms are subject to the definitive terms documented in the fund LPA and SAFE agreement, which govern in the event of any inconsistency with this document. Forward-looking statements about subsequent capital events are not commitments. Each future capital raise depends on execution results, market conditions, and the independent evaluation of each opportunity at the time of deployment.
