# KTV Property Brief

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## What KTV Is

KTV is the media layer of KaNeXT. Every game, every sermon, every campus event, every piece of content produced inside the ecosystem is captured, distributed, and monetized through KTV. It is not a streaming app. It is the owned media surface for every institution on the platform.

The content is not licensed or aggregated from third parties. It is produced by the institutions themselves as a function of operating on KaNeXT. A school plays a game and KTV captures it. A church holds a service and KTV streams it. A campus hosts a ceremony and KTV archives it. The content is created by institutional activity. KTV is where that content lives.

Every other media platform (YouTube, ESPN+, Facebook Live) requires institutions to push content outward to someone else's surface. KTV keeps it inside the ecosystem. KaNeXT owns the ad inventory. KaNeXT owns the data. KaNeXT owns the audience relationship. No algorithm decides who sees what. No third party sells ads against the content.

Three views across all modes: Featured (curated landing), Library (full searchable catalog), and Live (real-time streaming with auto-save to VOD). Chapter markers, speed controls, captions, casting, clip creation, series management, analytics, and sharing are universal features.

---

## How It Works Per Mode

**Sports.** Most sub-NCAA programs have zero broadcast infrastructure. Games are played in front of 200 people. Recruits cannot watch film. Parents in another state have no way to watch their child play. KTV gives every program their own broadcast network. Every game livestreamed and archived. Highlights auto-clipped. Players build recruiting reels from broadcasts. A podcast network gives programs a media voice they have never had.

KTV also serves as the Film Room inside the Dashboard. Video analysis with auto-tagging, telestration tools, playlists, side-by-side comparison, opponent film, and practice film. Film and broadcast live in the same infrastructure. A game broadcast on KTV is simultaneously archived as coaching film. There is no separate film tool. They are the same system.

**Community.** Churches upload sermons to YouTube where they sit next to conspiracy theories and unwanted ads. KTV gives every organization a clean, branded, ad-free media library. Sermons, worship recordings, teaching series, children's content, and radio broadcasts in one place, owned by them. Members find last week's message in one tap. Visitors watch before they ever walk in.

**Education.** Consolidates lectures, campus event recordings, and promotional content scattered across Zoom, Drive, and YouTube into one role-gated library.

**Business.** Consolidates demos, training, webinars, and investor updates. Gated content captures leads. Internal stays internal.

**Personal.** Creators own every viewer relationship. Subscriber-only gating. Direct monetization through KPay. No algorithm. No platform cut.

---

## The Dual Role in Athletics Mode

Most products separate broadcast from coaching film. KTV combines them in one governed system.

A game is livestreamed to fans through KTV. That same stream is auto-archived as VOD for anyone who missed it. That same video is simultaneously processed by KVision (the AI computer vision engine) into structured, intelligence-ready data: possessions segmented, timestamps generated, statistics extracted, player and lineup data attributed, actions tagged, and box scores constructed without human intervention.

The coaching staff accesses that same video through the Film Room tab in Dashboard with intelligence overlay, telestration, and analysis tools. The scouting staff pulls opponent broadcasts from KTV for game preparation. Players build highlight reels from the same content. Recruits watch the same broadcasts when evaluating the program.

One capture event. One video file. Broadcast, archive, film, intelligence, and recruiting content all from the same source. The data tier progression (V1 through V4, detailed in the Intelligence Architecture doc) is powered by this integration. KTV plus KVision is what makes automated intelligence data collection possible at scale.

---

## What It Replaces

KTV consolidates a fragmented landscape of video tools that institutions currently depend on:

In Sports: Hudl (film, $900-$3,300/year), FloSports and Pixellot (streaming subscriptions), YouTube (free but uncontrolled, ad-supported, algorithm-driven). KTV provides film, broadcast, highlight generation, podcast hosting, and scouting film exchange in one governed platform. Mandate institutions receive cameras and platform access as part of the governing body agreement (economics detailed in the Mandate Strategy doc).

In Community: YouTube (sermons next to uncontrolled content), Vimeo (paid hosting), scattered platform accounts. KTV provides a clean branded library with no ads, no algorithm, and institutional control.

In Education: Panopto, Kaltura, Zoom recordings, Google Drive. KTV consolidates all institutional video with role-based access control governing who sees what.

In Business and Personal: YouTube, Vimeo, Loom, Wistia. KTV consolidates with gating, analytics, and direct monetization through KPay.

---

## Content Compounding

The content library on KTV never shrinks. Every game ever played at every mandate institution is archived permanently. Every sermon, every campus event, every tournament is retrievable. A player's entire career lives on KTV. A coach can review years of an opponent's games. A scout can watch a prospect's development arc across multiple seasons.

The content library compounds across all modes simultaneously. The longer the platform operates, the deeper the archive, the more valuable the intelligence derived from it, and the harder it becomes for any competitor to replicate.

---

## Strategic Role in the OS

KTV serves three functions simultaneously:

It is the **distribution layer** that puts every institution's content in front of its community.

It is the **acquisition engine** that converts viewers into platform users. Every parent who watches a game is inside the app, one tap from a wallet, a phone number, and a merch store.

It is the **data ingestion layer** that feeds the intelligence system. Every game processed is every game evaluated, every player rated, every team analyzed.

The cameras capture. KVision processes. KTV distributes. The intelligence engines evaluate. KPay monetizes. KTV is not a streaming service added to KaNeXT. It is the media infrastructure that makes the mandate valuable, the intelligence possible, and the platform visible.

The mandate strategy, revenue model, and competitive positioning for KTV are detailed in their respective documents.

<!-- ============================================================ -->

# KPay Property Brief

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## What KPay Is

KPay is the financial layer of KaNeXT. Every user who downloads the app is onboarded into the wallet layer. The wallet ships on Day 1 with Apple Pay and Google Pay integration and the ability to send and receive money globally, subject to partner and regulatory coverage.

KPay is not a payment processor. It is a governed settlement system. The difference matters. A payment processor moves money. KPay governs why money moves, who authorized it, what rules constrain it, and where every dollar goes, then settles the transaction as a downstream consequence of a governed decision.

Every financial action inside KaNeXT follows a single canonical chain: Event, Rules, Authorization, Payment, Settlement, Audit. An Event is any institutional action that may create a financial obligation: a game, a payroll cycle, an NIL agreement, a fundraiser, a tuition payment, a tithe. Rules are constraints attached to that Event (authority, budget, eligibility, split/earmark, and compliance). Authorization captures who approved the decision. Payment executes the money movement. Settlement distributes the funds. The Audit Record is permanent and immutable.

No money moves unless a valid, governed Event exists. This chain is immutable and inspectable. Existing tools move money or report it after the fact. KPay is designed to govern the transaction chain before settlement, prevent violations before they occur, and produce the audit trail automatically as a function of settlement.

---

## How It Works Per Mode

**Sports.** Program budget tracking, NIL pool with compliance-documented payments, scholarship tracking, booster revenue reconciliation, vendor payments. When a parent buys a $20 ticket at a mandate institution, KPay checks whether the event is active, whether capacity remains, and whether the ticket type is valid. Upon settlement, the ledger entries are generated automatically (illustrative split: 80% to athletics operating budget, 10% to facilities fund, 5% to student life, 5% KaNeXT settlement fee). No human touched it. No accountant processed it. NIL payments are governed Events with contract prerequisites, compliance documentation requirements, and approval chains that must clear before a dollar moves. Player view: NIL earnings with tax documentation in one place.

**Education.** Tuition collection with installment plans, financial aid tracking and disbursement (aid disbursed directly into student wallets), scholarship fund management, department budgets, and institutional accounting. The wallet IS the student's campus card: dining, bookstore, vending, library printing, laundry, and all campus commerce through a tap or QR scan.

**Community.** Fund accounting with restricted/unrestricted enforcement at the transaction level. Money given to the building fund cannot be spent on payroll. The system prevents it. This is not a reporting feature. It is structural enforcement. Designated fund balances, tax receipt generation, clergy-specific payroll (housing allowance), and board-ready financial reports.

**Business.** Full double-entry accounting with chart of accounts. Accounts receivable with aging and auto-reminders. Accounts payable with approval workflows. Payroll with tax withholding and filing. Expense management with receipt capture and approval chains. Budget versus actual tracking. Exportable financial reports. E-commerce settlement from the Store tile auto-reconciles.

**Personal.** Every revenue stream in one wallet. Digital product sales, course revenue, services, subscriptions, tips, and affiliate commissions from the Earn tile all settle into one place. Tax dashboard with real-time estimates by category. Auto-save rules for taxes. Invoice creation. The KaNeXT Card lets creators spend earnings immediately.

---

## Wallet Acquisition

Every other fintech company spends billions acquiring wallet users through advertising. KaNeXT acquires them for free because the wallet is the financial consequence of every other layer doing its job.

A parent downloads the app to watch their child play on KTV. The wallet is already there. A student enrolls at a school network institution. The wallet is their campus card. A family member uses the VoIP layer to call internationally for free. They download the app. The wallet is there. They send money home at a fraction of what traditional remittance services charge. The recipient downloads the app. The wallet is there.

The mandate creates the audience. KTV creates the viewing funnel. The VoIP layer creates the international funnel. The school network creates captive institutional accounts. The bank provides the charter. KPay captures all of it. Incremental wallet acquisition cost is structurally near-zero relative to standalone fintech because adoption is bundled into institutional deployment.

---

## Commerce Economics

When a fan pays by card, KaNeXT charges 5% on the transaction. The card network takes approximately 3% underneath, leaving approximately 2% margin. When a fan pays from their KPay wallet, the transaction is closed-loop. The card network is eliminated. The full margin is captured, or KaNeXT passes savings to the user at 3%, still earning more than the card scenario while incentivizing wallet adoption.

Institutions do not switch to KPay because KaNeXT sells them on it. They switch because every transaction already flows through the KaNeXT settlement layer from the day the platform deploys. The only thing that changes over time is where the money moves: from external processors initially to internal wallet-to-wallet settlement as adoption grows. The governance does not change. Only the plumbing changes. The plumbing change reduces transaction costs dramatically for the institution.

---

## The Wallet as Product

The target wallet experience includes competitive APY on balances (rate dependent on banking partner and charter status), no minimum balance requirement, and no monthly fees.

The KaNeXT Card (virtual and physical) integrates with Apple Pay and Google Pay. In-ecosystem spending is closed-loop, wallet to wallet. Outside-ecosystem spending runs through the card network, with KaNeXT earning interchange on every transaction.

Target remittance pricing is a fraction of the global average cost of over 6%. International money transfer is a core feature, not an add-on. Actual rates are dependent on corridor, partner, and regulatory requirements. For diaspora communities connected to school network institutions and churches, competitive remittance rates are a primary driver of wallet adoption.

---

## Connection to the Bank Charter

KPay launches on white-label infrastructure from a licensed partner. The user sees KaNeXT branding only. KaNeXT simultaneously pursues its own bank charter through the acquisition described in the Bank Acquisition Brief. Once the charter is live, KPay migrates to KaNeXT-owned rails. The user experience does not change. The margin structure changes entirely.

Every wallet balance becomes a bank deposit. Every lending product originates from a KaNeXT-owned institution with platform-native underwriting data. Every payment settles through owned infrastructure. The bank charter transforms KPay from a financial product built on someone else's rails into a financial institution operating its own.

The bank acquisition strategy, deposit trajectory, and lending model are detailed in the Bank Acquisition Brief.

---

## What It Replaces

KPay consolidates a fragmented financial toolchain:

Peer-to-peer payments (Cash App, Venmo). Remittance (Western Union, at a fraction of the cost). Campus card systems and tuition payment portals. Church giving platforms (Tithe.ly, Pushpay). Accounting (QuickBooks). Payroll (Gusto, ADP). Payment processing (Stripe). E-commerce settlement (Shopify Payments). Expense management (Expensify). Creator payment platforms (Gumroad, Patreon payouts).

One wallet. One ledger. One audit trail. Every dollar governed from the moment the event that triggered it is created.

---

## Strategic Role in the OS

KPay is not a product added to KaNeXT. It is the reason KaNeXT exists as a business. Everything else is the funnel. The wallet is the business.

Every transaction across every mode flows through KPay. Tuition, tickets, merch, donations, payroll, NIL payments, subscriptions, remittance, tips, invoices, and e-commerce. The governed settlement chain is the architecture that makes institutional trust possible. Auditors can verify every transaction from source to destination. School boards, church governing bodies, and institutional leadership get accountability they can prove.

KPay creates structural virality. Payments to non-users prompt them to join in order to receive funds. The wallet spreads through institutional activity, not marketing.

Revenue model details are documented separately in the Revenue Model docs.

<!-- FILE: 05_The_Product/kvision_build_brief.md -->
<!-- ============================================================ -->

# KVision Build Brief

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## What KVision Is

KVision is KaNeXT's proprietary AI computer vision engine. It processes sports video into structured, intelligence-ready data. It is the link between the camera network and the intelligence system.

Without KVision, a camera captures a game and KTV streams it. That is a media product. With KVision, the same video is automatically processed into structured data: possessions segmented, timestamps generated, statistics extracted, player and lineup data attributed, actions tagged, and box scores constructed without human intervention. Every camera deployed becomes a data ingestion node. Every game broadcast is simultaneously a game evaluated.

KVision is built in-house. Full IP ownership. No third-party licensing risk. A multi-sport, fully owned, intelligence-native processing layer.

---

## What It Processes

KVision's processing pipeline extracts structured data at multiple levels of depth:

**Foundation layer.** Player detection, ball tracking, identity continuity across frames, team classification. This is the core that every downstream output depends on.

**Play-type classification.** Every possession is tagged by type: pick-and-roll, isolation, transition, post-up, spot-up, off-screen, cut, handoff, and other action types. Shot context is captured: catch-and-shoot versus off-the-dribble, contested versus open, pull-up versus layup versus dunk.

**Spatial data.** Court positioning, player movement patterns, spacing metrics, defensive positioning, closeout speed, defender proximity at point of release.

**Matchup tracking.** Defensive assignment per possession. Who is guarding whom. Assignment difficulty rating. Derived from defensive player positioning and movement response to offensive actions.

**Possession-level efficiency.** Points per possession by play type, by lineup, by matchup. Offensive and defensive efficiency segmented by action.

Every output is structured for direct ingestion by the intelligence engines: trait scoring, database enrichment, scouting, and simulation.

---

## The Data Tier System

The intelligence system operates across four data tiers. Each tier increases the confidence and accuracy of every intelligence output. KVision powers the upper tiers.

**V1 - Stats Only (Baseline).** StatKeeper manual input plus public box scores. No play-type data. Production-based KR only. Estimated usage patterns. This is the floor - every school starts here, and the intelligence still works. Lowest confidence tier but fully functional.

**V1+ - Licensed Granular (Bridge).** Everything in V1 plus third-party play-type data from Synergy or equivalent. Adds full classification triggers but no matchup tracking. KaNeXT does not own this data - it is licensed. This is the bridge between baseline and full intelligence.

**V2 - KVision Single Season (Year 1).** KaNeXT-owned cameras plus KVision processing. Everything changes here. Full play-type tagging, actual usage rates, matchup tracking, spatial data. High fidelity. Matchup importance activates. This is what a school gets in their first year on the KaNeXT platform. The data is owned by KaNeXT, not licensed from a third party.

**V3 - KVision Multi-Season (Year 2+).** Multiple seasons of KVision data plus full film archive. Trend analysis, system evolution tracking, and pattern recognition across years. Highest fidelity. The intelligence sees how players develop, how systems evolve, how coaching adjustments land over time. This is what a school gets by staying on the platform.

**The Flywheel.** V1 is what everyone has. V2 is what you get when you join KaNeXT. V3 is what you get when you stay. Data depth compounds over time. A school in Year 3 on the platform has intelligence that no competitor can replicate because no competitor has three years of KVision film on their roster.

---

## The StatKeeper Bridge

StatKeeper is the manual stat-tracking tool built into the KaNeXT OS Dashboard (Game Day tab). A team manager taps events during games in real time, producing live box scores and per-player stats. StatKeeper provides V1 data from day one without any camera infrastructure.

When KVision comes online, StatKeeper shifts from primary data source to validation and correction tool. The human-tagged data from StatKeeper provides ground truth that validates and trains KVision's automated output. Every game where a manager runs StatKeeper simultaneously with KVision processing generates labeled validation data that improves model accuracy.

This dual-input design means KVision does not need to be perfect on day one. StatKeeper provides the human correction layer that catches errors and feeds them back into model training. Over time, KVision accuracy improves and StatKeeper's role shifts from primary input to quality assurance.

---

## Three Layers of Value

### Layer 1: Free Infrastructure for Mandate and Network Schools

Every mandate institution and school network institution receives KVision processing at zero cost, included with the free cameras. This gives sub-NCAA schools the video-processing, tagging, tracking, and automated-output workflows that D1 programs currently purchase from Synergy Sports, Hudl, and comparable providers at significant annual cost. NBA teams pay millions annually for comparable data processing through Second Spectrum. Mandate institutions get it as part of the platform.

Schools that previously had no statistics beyond what a coach wrote on paper now receive automated data processing comparable to what elite programs use, from the same cameras that stream their games on KTV.

### Layer 2: Paid Product for Programs Outside the Mandate

KVision processing is offered as a standalone product to programs at any level: D1, D2, international professional leagues, national federations, development academies, and broadcast networks. These customers receive advanced data processing (player tracking, play tagging, possession classification, efficiency analysis, automated highlights) without access to KaNeXT's proprietary intelligence layer.

Programs currently spending significant annual budgets on Synergy, Hudl, and comparable video analytics products represent the addressable market.

### Layer 3: Data Input for KaNeXT Intelligence

KVision's processed data feeds the intelligence engines directly. The intelligence layer is never sold as part of KVision's standalone offering. Existing analytics providers (Second Spectrum, Synergy, Stats Perform) provide data: they track, tag, and classify. They do not evaluate, project, simulate, or govern. KaNeXT's intelligence engines do all of those things, using KVision data as input. KVision provides the data. KaNeXT provides the intelligence.

---

## The Training Data Advantage

KaNeXT deploys cameras to 1,000+ mandate institutions at full deployment. Every game filmed is processed by KVision. Every school running StatKeeper simultaneously generates human-labeled ground truth data that validates and trains KVision's models.

At scale: 1,000+ mandate institutions across 20+ games per sport per season produces 20,000+ games of labeled training data per year across every competitive level from NAIA to NJCAA to USCAA to NCCAA to select HS programs. This dataset covers levels of competition that no existing computer vision company has access to. SportsVU and Second Spectrum cover the NBA. Synergy covers D1. Nobody covers the mandate levels.

Every season, KVision's models improve across the exact population KaNeXT serves. The data moat compounds annually and cannot be replicated by any competitor without the institutional deployment infrastructure.

---

## Multi-Sport Expansion

KVision is architected to be sport-agnostic. The core pipeline (player detection, ball tracking, identity continuity, possession segmentation) is universal across all team sports. Sport-specific behavior lives in Sport Truth Adapters: modular classification layers that translate the core pipeline's raw detection output into sport-specific actions, events, and trait mappings. A basketball STA knows that a screen followed by a roll is a pick-and-roll. A football STA knows that a snap followed by a lateral is a pitch play. Same core pipeline, different classification vocabulary.

Basketball is the first Sport Truth Adapter. Football, volleyball, soccer, baseball, and additional sports follow the same pattern. Historical game film can be retroactively processed when cameras are installed, upgrading a program's data tier from V1 to V2 for archived games.

---

## Budget and Timeline

| Item | Allocation |
|---|---|
| CV/ML Engineering Team (4 engineers, 18 months) | $2.5M |
| Cloud Compute and Infrastructure | $0.7M |
| Training Data Labeling and QA | $0.4M |
| Contingency | $0.4M |
| **Total** | **$4.0M** |

| Milestone | Target |
|---|---|
| Engineering team hired | Month 1 |
| Foundation layer operational (box scores from film) | Month 3 |
| Classification layer V1 (play-type tagging, shot context) | Month 5 |
| V2 data tier fully operational | Month 6 |
| Mandate institution deployment begins | Month 6 |
| Multi-sport adapter (football) | Month 8 |
| Processing speed optimization (sub-2-hour turnaround) | Month 9 |
| V3 data tier operational (multi-season depth) | Month 12+ |

---

## Strategic Value

KVision completes the capture-to-intelligence pipeline: cameras capture, KVision processes, KaNeXT engines evaluate, KaNeXT OS governs.

Without this link, the camera network is a streaming service. With it, every camera deployed is a data ingestion node. The intelligence that runs on top of this data is KaNeXT's permanent competitive advantage.

# KPlay Property Brief

**KaNeXT LLC | Confidential**

---

## What KPlay Is

KPlay is the interactive layer of KaNeXT. It turns the intelligence system into products people play, learn from, train on, and compete in. Every game, every simulation, every course, and every interactive tool runs on the same governed intelligence architecture that evaluates real players, builds real rosters, and governs real institutions.

The separation from KTV is clear: KTV is watch. KPlay is do. A training video lives in KTV. A training course with quizzes and scenario decisions lives in KPlay. A game broadcast lives in KTV. College Basketball GM lives in KPlay.

KPlay is the one tile that breaks mode scoping. Content created in any mode is playable from any mode. The engine is universal. The content travels.

---

## Sports Management Games

This is the flagship product line and a significant commercial category within the OS.

Sports management is a proven commercial category. Titles like Football Manager and the EA Sports franchise have demonstrated sustained demand for deep management gameplay. KPlay sports management games are differentiated because they are built on the real KaNeXT intelligence system. The 54-trait evaluation system, the archetype classifications, the system fit computation, the KLVN normalization, and the possession-level simulation engine are not editorial approximations. They are the actual intelligence engines with a game interface on top.

**The portfolio covers every sport the intelligence system covers.** Basketball GM. Football GM. Soccer GM. Baseball GM. Softball GM. Volleyball GM. Each is a separate product with deep career-mode gameplay. A college basketball career spans hundreds of hours. The architecture is portable across every sport. Additional titles expand as the studio scales.

**Career depth spans every level.** A player starts in high school, gets recruited, plays college ball, enters the draft, and manages a pro career. Or they start as a high school coach, build a program, get hired at a college, recruit and develop players, and climb through the coaching ranks. The intelligence system governs every level with real competitive-level legends and KLVN normalization, so the gameplay experience at JUCO feels fundamentally different from D1, which feels fundamentally different from the pros. Current sports management titles are not built on a governed cross-level intelligence architecture like this.

**Real institutional mechanics.** Scholarship allocation with real budget constraints. NIL management with compliance rules. Transfer portal dynamics. Recruiting with system fit as a variable (not just star ratings). Real CBAs and salary cap structures at the pro level. Real transfer windows and loan systems in soccer. The governed settlement logic from KPay models real financial constraints inside the game. Players do not just manage a team. They manage an institution.

**Players are generated through the intelligence architecture.** The trait library, archetype system, development trajectories, and competitive-level legends create fictional players with realistic capability profiles shaped by the same frameworks that evaluate real athletes. The games do not use real player data. They use the real evaluation architecture to generate players that behave, develop, and interact the way real players do. This is the fundamental difference from every other sports management title on the market. Football Manager generates players from volunteer scout heuristics. EA uses editorial formulas. KPlay generates players from a governed intelligence system with 54 traits, position-specific weighting, system fit computation, and KLVN normalization across competitive levels. The depth of the generated players reflects the depth of the architecture underneath.

---

## Educational Games

KPlay produces educational titles in the tradition of Oregon Trail: interactive experiences where the player makes consequential decisions and learns through outcome, not instruction.

The difference is that KPlay games are intelligent. The decision trees are not static scripts. The intelligence engines adapt scenarios, compute consequences, and model outcomes the same way they model real institutional decisions. A financial literacy game does not just say "you spent too much and went bankrupt." It models the actual financial dynamics, shows why the decision failed, and lets the player try alternate strategies with the simulation engine computing different outcomes each time.

**Titles span every educational domain.** History, civics, financial literacy, science, geography, and faith-based values. Schools used to pay significant amounts for educational software that was barely interactive. KPlay makes it genuinely intelligent because the same engines that simulate real outcomes power the games.

**Millsberry-style tycoon and simulation games.** Run a business from startup to scale. Manage an office. Build a campus. Operate a hospital. These are not toy simulations. The hiring intelligence engine evaluates candidates. The financial simulation runs on governed settlement logic. The team composition engine models how people work together. Kids learn business, finance, and management by making real decisions inside real intelligence frameworks.

**Family-safe and curriculum-aligned.** The content is wholesome. Schools in the network integrate games into coursework. Churches offer them to youth programs. Families access them alongside the sports content their children already consume. Every casual session is a session inside the KaNeXT ecosystem.

---

## Professional Training and the Learning Lab

KPlay is not just entertainment and education. It is a professional training environment.

**The Learning Lab** is the professional application of the intelligence engines without the entertainment wrapper. Four rooms:

The Film Room overlays intelligence on real game footage. Every possession tagged, every player rated, every decision annotated with KR data and system context.

The War Room generates scouting reports and runs game-preparation simulations against real upcoming opponents with real data.

The Simulation Sandbox provides unrestricted engine access. Build any roster, run any matchup, simulate any season, test any system change, model any cap scenario.

The Development Lab tracks longitudinal player development and projects future performance across competitive levels.

Coaches, scouts, front office professionals, and students interact directly with the intelligence engines. The Learning Lab is a competitive weapon for practitioners and an academic tool for students studying sports management, analytics, or institutional operations.

**Business training uses the same principle.** A new hire at a company completes an interactive onboarding course built on KPlay. A sales team practices objection handling through AI-powered role-play with Dipson. A compliance officer works through real scenarios with real consequences computed by the simulation engine. A financial officer trains on budget simulations that use the same governed settlement logic as actual KPay transactions.

**Certification programs.** KPlay powers professional certification: coaching certification, scouting certification, intelligence system certification, institutional operations certification. Interactive assessment, not just exams. The certification proves the person can operate inside the intelligence framework, not just answer questions about it.

---

## Business Education and Academic Programs

The intelligence architecture is deep enough to be curriculum.

**Sports Business as a degree program.** A student managing a simulated athletic department learns budgeting, personnel management, marketing, compliance, and strategic planning through the same engines that manage real programs. But because the intelligence system covers 50+ intelligence domains, the curriculum goes far beyond sports. Player evaluation teaches data-driven assessment methodology. Team composition teaches portfolio construction. System fit teaches organizational alignment. Simulation teaches scenario modeling and decision-making under uncertainty. Scholarship and NIL allocation teaches resource optimization. These are transferable skills that apply to any institution, not just athletics.

**General business and institutional management.** The intelligence extends to admissions, hiring, acquisitions, and real estate. A student who learns to evaluate a recruit using the KR pipeline can evaluate a job candidate using the same architecture. A student who learns to model roster construction can model team composition in a corporate environment. A student who learns to simulate game outcomes can simulate market scenarios. The intelligence system teaches institutional reasoning, not just sports reasoning.

**Degree programs schools in the network can offer:** Sports Business and Analytics. Institutional Operations and Management. Business Administration with simulation-driven coursework. Data-Driven Decision Making. Each program uses the intelligence engines as the learning environment and KPlay as the delivery platform.

The learning environment is powered by KPlay. The content is delivered through KTV. The financial transactions flow through KPay. Every layer of KaNeXT participates in the delivery of a single educational product.

Schools in the network can offer this curriculum through their existing accreditation. A student at a network school in the Midwest accesses the same simulation environment as a student on the flagship campus. The intelligence is the education. The depth of the architecture is the depth of the curriculum.

---

## How It Works Per Mode

**Sports.** Management games, tactical draw tools, player IQ courses, life skills training (NIL financial literacy, media training), pick'em and bracket competitions, fantasy leagues, trivia, coach scenario training with AI feedback.

**Education.** Interactive learning beyond the LMS. Virtual labs and simulations. Study games and exam prep. Career path simulators. Financial literacy simulators. Faculty build interactive content supplementing lectures.

**Community.** Bible trivia and scripture games. Youth ministry interactive content. Leadership development courses. Volunteer training with scenarios.

**Business.** Interactive product demos. Customer onboarding courses. Certification programs. Sales role-play with AI. Compliance training. Employee training experiences.

**Personal.** Creators build and sell courses, interactive tools, and premium content through the Earn tile. Revenue settles through KPay.

---

## The Intelligence Advantage

Existing interactive products in every category (sports games, educational software, business training, simulation tools) are built on static content or editorial inputs. Football Manager uses volunteer scouts. Educational games use scripted decision trees. Business training uses canned scenarios.

KPlay runs on the real KaNeXT intelligence architecture. The evaluation pipeline is real. The simulation engine resolves outcomes through real system-versus-system and archetype-versus-archetype interaction models. Generated players are shaped by the same trait libraries, legends, and normalization that govern real evaluations. The intelligence feeds the games with a depth of architectural logic that editorial-based competitors cannot match.

The games also teach the intelligence back to users. A person who plays Basketball GM for hundreds of hours learns what system fit means, how archetypes interact, why a high-KR player can fail in the wrong system, and how roster construction works as a structural problem. They become more sophisticated consumers of the intelligence products. The intelligence makes the games deeper. The games make the audience smarter.

---

## Strategic Role in the OS

KPlay is not a game studio bolted onto a platform. It is the interactive expression of the intelligence architecture.

Games sell the OS. A coach's child plays Basketball Manager for hundreds of hours, learns the evaluation language intuitively, and recognizes the same system when their parent's program deploys KaNeXT. Games pre-educate fans. A viewer who plays Soccer Manager already understands KR ratings, system fit, and archetype classification before encountering the intelligence in a real institutional context. Games teach the intelligence. Users learn advanced stats, evaluation thinking, system fit, and archetype reasoning through gameplay, making them more sophisticated consumers of the intelligence products.

The mandate delivers the audience. The intelligence architecture powers the content. The games, courses, and simulations keep users inside the ecosystem between the high-engagement moments of watching games and managing institutional operations. Every session inside KPlay is a session inside KaNeXT.

Revenue model details are documented separately.

# KStat - Live Data Capture Engine

## What KStat Is

KStat is the real-time stat tracking system inside KaNeXT OS. It lives in Dashboard > Game Day in Athletics mode. Every tap a stat keeper makes during a live game feeds the intelligence system, the coaching staff, the broadcast, and the fan experience simultaneously. One tap creates seven downstream outputs.

KStat is not a scorekeeping app. GameChanger is a scorekeeping app. KStat is a data capture layer that turns live athletic events into structured intelligence. The difference is what happens after the stat is entered. In GameChanger, a stat becomes a box score. In KStat, a stat becomes a KR update, a halftime coaching packet, a postgame media report, a live broadcast overlay, a recruiting data point, a development tracking input, and a financial trigger for play-based pledges. One tap, seven systems.

## The Problem KStat Solves

The invisible athlete problem is the foundational gap in college athletics below the Power Five. There are over 500,000 college athletes in the United States. Fewer than 10% play at programs with dedicated analytics staff, professional stat tracking, or video analysis infrastructure. The remaining 90% play at programs where stats are kept on paper, entered into spreadsheets after games, and never connected to anything downstream. Their production data exists in fragments that no system can consume.

This means 450,000+ athletes are invisible to the intelligence system. Their stats do not exist in a form that can be evaluated, compared, or projected. Their coaches cannot generate scouting reports because opponent data is equally fragmented. Their fans cannot follow games in real time because there is no live data feed. Their SIDs (Sports Information Directors) - if the program even has one - spend hours manually producing box scores and recaps that a system could generate in seconds.

KStat solves this by making data capture so simple that any student manager, volunteer parent, or operations assistant can do it during a live game. Two taps: select player, select stat. No training required. No analytics background needed. The system handles everything downstream.

## How It Works

KStat operates in three phases during every game.

**Setup.** Select home and away teams (auto-populated from Roster if it is your game). Choose game type: Regular Season, Conference, Tournament, or Scrimmage. Set half length. Tap players to toggle starter/bench status. The game starts when both teams have exactly five starters marked.

**Live Tracking.** Portrait mode, designed for one-handed operation on the bench. Scoreboard at top shows home score, away score, period, and game clock with play/pause controls. Player selection row displays numbered circles for home and away players. The selected player is highlighted. Stat buttons below: 3pt make/miss, 2pt make/miss, FT make/miss, DefReb, OffReb, TO, STL, AST, BLK, Sub, Foul. Two-tap flow: tap player, tap stat. No confirmation dialogs during live play. Play-by-play feed shows the last three entries. Undo button for corrections. Substitution overlay shows On Court and Bench columns for tap-to-swap. Foul overlay offers Personal, Shooting, Offensive, Technical, and Flagrant options.

**Box Score.** Auto-generated from live data. Final score, full stat table per team with every standard stat column, team totals, horizontal scroll with player names fixed. Export to JSON, CSV, or PDF.

## The Seven Downstream Outputs

Every stat tap creates data that flows to seven systems simultaneously.

**1. Live Box Score.** Updates automatically during the game. Coaches on the bench see real-time stats on their phone or tablet. No waiting for halftime printouts.

**2. Halftime Staff Packet.** At the halftime buzzer, Dipson auto-generates a coaching packet using first-half KStat data and the intelligence files. Contents include a top-3 decision summary (problem-to-adjustment format), game state dashboard (score, pace, fouls, turnovers, points per possession), Five Factors analysis (eFG%, turnover rate, offensive rebounding rate, free throw rate, transition), plan adherence check against the pregame scouting report, opponent offensive and defensive analysis, lineup and matchup data with plus-minus, and an adjustments sandbox with 2-5 defensive and 2-5 offensive options ranked by projected impact. Delivered to coaching staff through Dipson or Messages. Confidence percentage based on data tier.

**3. Postgame Staff Packet.** At the final buzzer, Dipson auto-generates a full postgame analysis: complete box score with advanced stats, Five Factors final, plan adherence audit, opponent analysis, lineup analysis (every combination with plus-minus and minutes), player grades against expectations, teaching clips auto-tagged (top 5 positive moments, top 5 correctable moments linked to Film Room if the game was recorded), development notes, and a preview of the next opponent. Archived for season-long trend tracking.

**4. Media Game Report.** Dipson auto-generates an ESPN-style game recap in professional sports writing tone. Headline, game summary paragraph, player of the game with context, key stats comparison table, and simplified box score. Publishing options: auto-post to Social, share to KTV as graphic overlay, export PDF for media distribution, email to local media contacts. School SID can review before publishing, or programs without an SID can set it to auto-publish. This eliminates the SID bottleneck for small programs that cannot afford dedicated media staff.

**5. Live Broadcast Overlay.** During games broadcast on KTV, KStat feeds the live score overlay, player stat graphics, and play-by-play updates to the broadcast in real time. Fans watching on KTV see an ESPN-quality production powered by one person tapping a phone.

**6. Intelligence System Feed.** Every game's data flows into the KaNeXT Intelligence pipeline. Player KR updates after every game based on new production data. Team KR recalculates. System identity (OSIE/DSIE) refines at five-game checkpoints. BPR (Basketball Performance Rating) computes per-game impact. The more games tracked through KStat, the more accurate every evaluation becomes. This is the data flywheel: KStat captures data, the intelligence system consumes data, intelligence quality improves, the product becomes more valuable, more programs adopt KStat.

**7. Financial Triggers.** Play-based pledges in the Booster tile auto-resolve from KStat data. A fan who pledged "$2 per three-pointer" sees their pledge auto-charged through KPay when the final buzzer sounds. Fan Challenges (prediction games between fans) auto-resolve using the same data. No human intervention needed because the stat data is live and structured.

## Multi-Sport Expansion

KStat follows the same two-tap architecture across every sport with sport-specific stat button configurations. The build order reflects market priority and technical complexity.

Phase 1: Basketball (complete). Phase 2: Soccer and Flag Football. Phase 3: Volleyball, Hockey, and Lacrosse. Phase 4: Golf, Tennis, Track and Field, Cheerleading/STUNT, and Swimming and Diving. Phase 5: Football and Baseball. Phase 6: Wrestling and Boxing.

14 build specifications covering 26 sport configurations are complete. Each sport loads its own stat button layout, scoring rules, and period structure while sharing the same underlying data pipeline and downstream output architecture. Adding a new sport is a configuration problem, not an architecture problem.

## The Data Tier Ladder

KStat creates a natural upgrade path that compounds data value over time.

V1 (Stats-Only) is where every program starts. Public box scores, roster data, season stats. Production-based KR evaluations. Available for every organized program, even those not on the KaNeXT platform, through public data scraping.

V1+ (Licensed Granular) adds third-party play-type data when available. Fuller evaluations possible but KaNeXT does not own the data.

V2 (KVision - 1 Season) is what programs get when they join KaNeXT and deploy cameras. KaNeXT-owned data: full play-type tagging, actual usage tracking, matchup data, spatial analysis. Full KR evaluations with high confidence. First year on the platform.

V3 (KVision Deep - Multi-Season) is what programs get when they stay. Multiple seasons of owned data create trend analysis, pattern recognition, historical comparison, and the highest confidence evaluations. The intelligence compounds.

V1 is free. V2 requires KaNeXT. V3 requires loyalty. Each tier produces meaningfully better intelligence, creating natural lock-in through data depth rather than contracts.

## Competitive Landscape

**GameChanger** (DICK'S Sporting Goods). Free for coaches, $9.99/month for fans. 550K+ reviews, the dominant youth sports app. Covers 20+ sports. Strengths: massive user base, simple interface, live streaming, free for coaches. Weakness: stats are terminal - they produce box scores and highlight reels but do not feed an intelligence system, do not generate coaching packets, do not trigger financial events, do not evaluate players. GameChanger is a consumer product for parents. KStat is an institutional intelligence layer for coaches.

**Hudl** ($900-3,300/year). The standard for game film. Acquired FastModel Sports (FastDraw, FastScout, FastRecruit) in November 2025. Strengths: ubiquitous in college and high school, strong film tools, now has play diagramming through FastDraw acquisition. Weakness: film-first, not stat-first. Hudl does not do live stat tracking. It does not generate coaching packets. It does not evaluate players. It does not connect to financial systems. Hudl is a video platform. KStat feeds video intelligence (through KTV and Film Room) but also feeds the entire KaNeXT intelligence pipeline.

**Synergy Sports** (owned by Sportradar). The gold standard for play-type analytics at the professional and Power Five level. Strengths: deep play-type data, proprietary tagging. Weakness: expensive, only available at the highest levels, no integration with broader institutional systems. Synergy serves the top 5% of programs. KStat serves the other 95%.

**SportsCloud / iStat / manual scorebooks.** Various small stat tracking tools used at lower levels. None connect to an intelligence system. None generate downstream outputs. None feed financial triggers. They are digital versions of paper scorebooks.

KStat's competitive position: it is the only stat tracking tool that turns every tap into seven simultaneous downstream outputs across coaching intelligence, media production, broadcast, financial operations, and player evaluation. The competition tracks stats. KStat captures institutional intelligence.

## The Network Effect

Every program that uses KStat adds data to the player pool. When Lincoln University tracks stats through KStat, every Lincoln player's data enters the pool. When Lincoln's conference opponent tracks through KStat, the entire conference's data deepens. When Dipson evaluates a Lincoln player, it uses both Lincoln's data and every opponent's data. The more programs on KStat, the more accurate every evaluation becomes for every program.

This creates a data network effect where the product becomes more valuable for existing users as new users join - the defining characteristic of platform businesses that achieve winner-take-all market dynamics.

## Revenue Impact

KStat is not a standalone revenue product. It is the data capture layer that makes the entire intelligence system valuable. Without live data flowing in, the intelligence files are static reference documents. With KStat feeding data from thousands of games per season, the intelligence system becomes a living, self-improving evaluation engine.

KStat drives revenue through four channels. First, it is a key feature of the KaNeXT OS platform subscription (institutions pay for the OS, KStat is included). Second, it powers KTV game broadcasts (every broadcast requires a stat feed, every broadcast pulls parents into the app, every parent is one tap from a wallet). Third, it triggers financial activity in Booster (play-based pledges and Fan Challenges generate giving that would not exist without live stat data). Fourth, it produces the data that makes KaNeXT Intelligence licensing valuable to third parties (intelligence without fresh data is static; intelligence with KStat data is alive).

<!-- FILE: 05_The_Product/kdraw_product_brief.md -->
<!-- ============================================================ -->

# KDraw - Play Diagramming and Playbook Intelligence

## What KDraw Is

KDraw is the play diagramming and playbook management tool inside KaNeXT OS. It lives in Dashboard > Scouting in Athletics mode and in KPlay as a coaching tool. Coaches draw, animate, organize, and share plays and drills from their phone, tablet, or desktop. Every play created is immediately available to Dipson, the Scouting tab, the Film Room, KPlay, and every other component of the platform.

KDraw replaces FastDraw (FastModel Sports, now owned by Hudl), The Hoops Geek Play Creator, FastBreak PlayBook, and physical coaching whiteboards. It launches with basketball and expands to football, soccer, hockey, volleyball, and lacrosse.

## The Problem KDraw Solves

Play diagramming is one of the most universal coaching activities in sports. Every basketball coach in America diagrams plays - on whiteboards, napkins, iPads, or dedicated software. FastDraw (now Hudl's FastDraw) has been the industry standard for two decades, used by nearly every NBA and NCAA team. But FastDraw and every other diagramming tool share the same fundamental limitation: plays are isolated files.

A coach draws a play in FastDraw. That play lives in FastDraw. It does not connect to the scouting report. It does not connect to the game film where that play was actually executed. It does not connect to the simulation engine that projects outcomes. It does not connect to the player development plan. It does not connect to the practice plan. It does not connect to the playbook the players study on their phones. It does not connect to the intelligence system that knows which plays work against which defensive systems.

The coach draws the play in one app, writes the scouting report in another app, watches the film in a third app, builds the practice plan in a fourth app, sends the playbook to players through a fifth app, and tracks execution data in a sixth app. Six tools, zero integration, zero intelligence.

KDraw solves this by making every play a shared data object inside the KaNeXT OS. Draw a play, and Dipson can reference it by name in a scouting report. Tag a film possession, and KDraw shows which play was called. Assign a play to a player in KPlay, and the player studies it with step-by-step animation on their phone. Run a simulation against an upcoming opponent, and KDraw's plays are the offensive options tested. Build a practice plan in Calendar, and KDraw's plays are the drills attached. The play is not a file. It is a connected intelligence object.

## Core Features

**Drawing Engine.** Full court and half court diagrams. Offensive and defensive player markers (numbered circles, customizable). Drag-and-drop player positioning. Movement lines for cuts (solid arrows), screens (X marks), dribble paths (wavy arrows), passes (dashed lines), and shooting zones. Court templates sized by competition level and court dimensions. Color customization for visual clarity.

**Animation System.** Step through play execution frame by frame. Each frame represents a moment in the play's progression. FastBuild-style auto-advance moves players to their next position. Play back the full animation at adjustable speed. The animation is what transforms a static diagram into a teaching tool - players see the play unfold rather than interpreting a cluttered diagram.

**Playbook Organization.** Plays organized by category: offense (sets, quick hitters, motion reads, continuity), defense (man principles, zone alignments, press schemes, trap triggers), special situations (BLOB/baseline out of bounds, SLOB/sideline out of bounds, ATO/after timeout, press break, last shot), and drills (individual, small group, team). Search by name, tag, category, or situation. Playbook export as PDF for printing or as shareable digital playbook.

**Sharing and Distribution.** Share individual plays or entire playbooks through Messages to coaching staff or players. Players receive plays in their KPlay view as required study material with step-by-step animation. Export plays as images (for social media, presentations, or print) or as animated GIFs. Embed plays in scouting reports generated by Dipson.

## Integration Points - The Competitive Moat

The integration between KDraw and the rest of the KaNeXT OS is the competitive advantage that no standalone diagramming tool can replicate. These are not theoretical integrations. They are architectural connections built into the platform.

**KDraw to Dipson.** When Dipson generates a scouting report for an upcoming opponent, it can reference specific plays from the coach's playbook. "Against their 2-3 zone, consider running your Flex Zone set (Play #14). In 8 possessions this season, this set has produced 1.12 PPP against zone defenses." Dipson knows the play because it is a data object in the system, not a file on a laptop.

**KDraw to Film Room.** When coaches tag film possessions in the Film Room, they can link each possession to the play that was called. "This possession was our Horns set." Over a season, this builds a database of play-call-to-outcome data: which plays produce the most points per possession, which plays break down against specific defenses, which players execute which plays most effectively. This data feeds Dipson's coaching recommendations and the Simulation Engine.

**KDraw to Scouting.** The Scouting tab can attach play suggestions to matchup analysis. "Against their Pack Line defense, your Dribble Drive series has averaged 0.95 PPP this season. Consider increasing usage from 15% to 25% of half-court possessions." The plays referenced are KDraw plays, viewable with one tap.

**KDraw to KPlay.** Plays assigned to players appear in their KPlay learning environment as interactive study material. Players step through the animation, read coach notes attached to each frame, and confirm completion. Coaches can assign specific plays as homework before games or practices. Completion tracking shows who studied and who did not.

**KDraw to Calendar (Practice Plans).** When coaches build practice plans in Calendar, they attach KDraw plays and drills directly to practice segments. "7:00-7:15 PM: Install Horns Counter (KDraw Play #22). 7:15-7:30 PM: 3-on-3 Shell Drill (KDraw Drill #8)." Players see the practice plan with playable animations for each segment.

**KDraw to Simulation.** When the Simulation Engine projects game outcomes against an upcoming opponent, it uses play-level data. If KDraw plays are tagged to film possessions, the system knows the expected points per possession for each play type against each defensive system. This makes simulations granular: not just "we project 74 points" but "if we run Horns at 20% usage against their ICE coverage, we project 0.98 PPP on those possessions."

## Multi-Sport Expansion

KDraw launches with basketball because basketball coaches are the most active play diagrammers and the market is most established. Expansion follows the same principle as KStat: each sport loads its own field/court template and position markers while sharing the same drawing engine, animation system, organization structure, and integration architecture.

**Football** (Phase 2): Formation diagrams with offensive and defensive fronts. Route trees with individual route assignments. Blocking schemes. Coverage shells. Play-action concepts. The football market for diagramming is even larger than basketball because of the complexity of 11-on-11 schemes.

**Soccer** (Phase 2): Set piece diagrams (corners, free kicks, throw-ins). Tactical shape illustrations (pressing triggers, build-up patterns, transition shapes). Small-sided drill designs.

**Hockey** (Phase 3): Breakout patterns. Power play setups. Penalty kill formations. Forecheck systems. Neutral zone structures.

**Volleyball** (Phase 3): Rotation diagrams. Serve-receive formations. Blocking schemes. Offensive play sets by rotation.

**Lacrosse** (Phase 3): Offensive formations. Ride and clear patterns. Man-up/man-down sets. Defensive slides.

Each sport expansion is a configuration deployment, not a new product build. The drawing engine, animation system, and integration points are universal.

## Competitive Landscape

**FastDraw (Hudl/FastModel Sports).** The 20-year incumbent. Used by nearly every NBA and NCAA team. Over 9,000 community-shared plays. Strengths: brand recognition, massive play library, professional quality output, now integrated with Hudl's film platform after the November 2025 acquisition. Weakness: desktop-first design (the iPad app has not been meaningfully updated since 2016), no connection to an intelligence system, no live play-to-outcome tracking, no AI integration, plays are files not data objects. The Hudl acquisition should improve film-to-diagram integration, but it cannot create the intelligence layer that connects plays to evaluations, simulations, and coaching packets. FastDraw Advanced pricing is enterprise-only (contact sales), creating a cost barrier for small programs.

**The Hoops Geek Play Creator.** Modern mobile-first alternative. Clean interface, FastDraw import capability, affordable pricing, growing community library. Strengths: mobile-native, good UX, aggressive pricing. Weakness: standalone tool with no ecosystem integration. Plays do not connect to film, scouting, intelligence, or any downstream system.

**FastBreak PlayBook.** Another modern alternative with football support. Team-based collaboration, no user caps, athletic department discounts. Strengths: multi-sport (basketball and football), team pricing model. Weakness: same standalone limitation - plays are isolated from every other coaching tool.

**Physical Whiteboards and Napkins.** Still the most common "tool" for the majority of coaches worldwide. Zero cost, zero integration, zero ability to share digitally, zero ability to animate, zero persistence (the whiteboard gets erased after practice).

KDraw's competitive position: it is the only play diagramming tool embedded inside an operating system with AI intelligence, live stat tracking, film analysis, scouting reports, simulation projections, player development, and financial operations. Every competitor draws plays. KDraw draws plays that the entire institution can consume, reference, track, and learn from.

## Why This Matters for Investors

Play diagramming is a universal coaching behavior with a captive market. Every basketball program in America diagrams plays. FastDraw has proven the market exists and is willing to pay for digital tools. Hudl's acquisition of FastModel in November 2025 validates the strategic value of coaching workflow tools.

KDraw enters this market with three structural advantages. First, it is mobile-native from day one (FastDraw's mobile app has not been updated since 2016, and the primary product is desktop software). Second, it is integrated into an operating system rather than standing alone, which means every play connects to seven other systems. Third, it is powered by an intelligence layer that no competitor has - Dipson can recommend plays based on opponent tendencies, track play execution effectiveness over time, and connect play calls to statistical outcomes.

The acquisition cost for KDraw is zero because it is included in the KaNeXT OS platform. Programs do not pay separately for it. This undercuts every competitor's pricing model while delivering more functionality. The revenue model is institutional: programs pay for the OS, and KDraw is one of the reasons they pay.

The multi-sport expansion path follows the same market logic as KStat. Basketball first (proven market, highest coaching tool adoption), then football (largest participation sport, complex scheme requirements create high demand for diagramming tools), then the remaining sports. Each expansion deepens the platform's value to athletic departments that run multiple sports programs.

<!-- FILE: 05_The_Product/universal_rbac_constitution_v2.md -->
<!-- ============================================================ -->

# KaNeXT Universal RBAC Constitution

**Version 2.0 - April 2026 - LOCKED**

---

## 1. Universal Constitution

This is the governing ladder across every mode. It does not decide the exact screen someone sees. It decides their power level in the system.

| Level | Authority | Scope | Visibility | Decision |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 0 | Observer | Personal | Public | None |
| 1 | Personal | Sub-domain | Community | Self |
| 2 | Execution | Program | Tactical | Operational |
| 3 | Program Governance | Domain | Competitive | Tactical |
| 4 | Domain Governance | Global | Strategic | Strategic |
| 5 | Institutional | Institutional | Institutional | Institutional |

**Plain-English meaning:**

- Level 0 = outside observer, mostly public-only
- Level 1 = can manage self or personal actions
- Level 2 = can do actual work in the system
- Level 3 = can run a program or department
- Level 4 = can oversee a major domain
- Level 5 = full institutional authority

---

## 2. Universal Role Ladder

Every user in the system maps to one of 7 universal roles. These roles determine power level. The mode-specific template determines what that power level looks and feels like.

| Role | Label | Authority Level | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | 5 - Institutional | Full system authority. Creates modes, assigns roles, sees everything. |
| R1 | Top Leader | 4 - Domain Governance | Runs the institution or organization. Strategic decisions, full visibility across all domains. |
| R2 | Department Head | 3 - Program Governance | Runs a program or department. Competitive intelligence, tactical decisions within their domain. |
| R3 | Staff | 2 - Execution | Executes work within the system. Tactical visibility scoped to their lane. Operational decisions only. |
| R4 | Member | 1 - Personal | Active participant. Manages self. Sees own data, community-level visibility. |
| R5 | Follower | 0 - Observer | Passive engagement. Community-level visibility. No decision authority. |
| R6 | Public | 0 - Observer | No relationship to the organization. Public-only visibility. No decisions. |

**Key distinction between R5 and R6:** A Follower has chosen to engage (they follow, subscribe, attend). Public has no relationship at all. Both sit at Observer authority, but Followers may see community-level content that pure Public cannot.

---

## 3. Mode-Specific Role Templates

The universal role ladder tells you how much power someone has. The mode-specific template tells you WHO they are in that environment and WHAT they see.

Two people on the same universal level get completely different app experiences depending on the mode.

| Role | Universal Label | Athletics | Business | Education | Community | Personal |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Owner | Owner | Owner | Owner | Owner |
| R1 | Top Leader | AD | CEO | President | Senior Leader | You |
| R2 | Department Head | Head Coach | VP | Dean | Director | - |
| R3 | Staff | Asst Coach | Manager | Faculty | Leader | - |
| R4 | Member | Player | Customer | Student | Member | Subscriber |
| R5 | Follower | Fan | Investor | Alumni / Parent / Board | Attendee / Visitor | Follower |
| R6 | Public | Public | Public | Public | Public | Public |

---

## 4. Mode Breakdowns

### Athletics Mode

| Role | Template | Authority | What They See | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Institutional | Everything. All teams, all sports, all intelligence, all financials, all operations. | Full system control. |
| R1 | AD | Domain Governance | All sports programs, budgets, compliance, strategic metrics, KR (full), recruiting pipeline. | Strategic decisions across athletic department. Hires coaches. Sets policy. |
| R2 | Head Coach | Program Governance | Own team roster, KR (full for own players), scouting, game ops, recruiting, scholarship allocation, film. | Tactical decisions for their program. Lineup, recruiting offers, development plans. |
| R3 | Asst Coach | Execution | Own team roster (scoped), KR (bands only), film, practice plans, assigned recruiting territory. | Operational tasks. Runs practice, scouts assigned targets, enters data. |
| R4 | Player | Personal | Own profile, own stats, own development plan, own KR (partial - self only), team schedule, community feed. | Self-management. Updates availability, reviews own film, tracks own progress. |
| R5 | Fan | Observer | Public schedule, scores, highlights, player profiles (public), team feed, merchandise. | No decisions. Follows, watches, purchases. |
| R6 | Public | Observer | Public schedule, scores, highlights. | None. |

**KR Visibility:** R0-R2 = full KR. R3 = bands only. R4 = partial self-only. R5-R6 = hidden.

### Business Mode

| Role | Template | Authority | What They See | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Institutional | Everything. All company data, financials, governance, strategy, cap table. | Full system control. |
| R1 | CEO | Domain Governance | All departments, financials (exact), strategy, governance, team performance, investor relations. | Strategic decisions. Hires VPs. Sets company direction. |
| R2 | VP | Program Governance | Own department, budget (exact), team metrics, competitive intelligence relevant to their domain. | Tactical decisions for their department. Allocates resources, sets targets. |
| R3 | Manager | Execution | Own team, operational metrics, project dashboards, task management. | Operational decisions. Manages team output, runs projects. |
| R4 | Customer | Personal | Own account, own usage, own billing, product features, support. | Self-management. Uses the product. |
| R5 | Investor | Observer | Data room (scoped by investor type), financials (exact for strategic, banded for retail), board pack (if board member). | No operational decisions. Reviews performance, provides governance input if board. |
| R6 | Public | Observer | Public website, marketing materials, press releases. | None. |

**Financial Visibility:** R0-R2 = exact. R3 = department-scoped. R4 = own billing only. R5 = exact for strategic investors and board, banded for retail. R6 = hidden.

### Education Mode

| Role | Template | Authority | What They See | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Institutional | Everything. All academic programs, financials, enrollment, compliance, accreditation. | Full system control. |
| R1 | President | Domain Governance | All departments, enrollment pipeline, financials, accreditation status, strategic metrics, housing, athletics link. | Strategic decisions. Appoints deans. Sets institutional direction. |
| R2 | Dean | Program Governance | Own school or division, faculty, curriculum, student performance, admissions (for their programs), budget. | Tactical decisions for their academic domain. Hires faculty. Approves curriculum. |
| R3 | Faculty | Execution | Own courses, own students (grades, attendance), academic calendar, advising caseload. | Operational decisions. Grades, advises, teaches. |
| R4 | Student | Personal | Own grades, own schedule, own financial aid, own housing, campus life, community feed, own athletic profile (if athlete). | Self-management. Registers for courses, pays tuition, manages campus life. |
| R5 | Alumni / Parent / Board | Observer | Public programs, events, giving history (own), alumni network. Board members see governance pack. Parents see student-shared data only. | No operational decisions. Donates, networks, provides governance input if board. |
| R6 | Public | Observer | Public website, program listings, admissions info, campus events. | None. |

**FERPA Note:** Student data (grades, financial aid, disciplinary) is visible only to the student (R4 self) and authorized institutional staff (R2-R3 in their lane, R1, R0). Parents see only what the student explicitly shares.

### Community Mode

| Role | Template | Authority | What They See | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Institutional | Everything. All ministries/programs, financials, giving, membership, operations. | Full system control. |
| R1 | Senior Leader | Domain Governance | All programs, giving reports, membership, growth metrics, strategic planning, compliance. | Strategic decisions. Appoints directors. Sets organizational vision. |
| R2 | Director | Program Governance | Own ministry or program area, volunteers, events, budget for their area, participation metrics. | Tactical decisions for their program. Plans events, manages volunteers. |
| R3 | Leader | Execution | Own team or small group, event logistics, volunteer coordination, attendance. | Operational decisions. Runs events, leads groups, coordinates volunteers. |
| R4 | Member | Personal | Own profile, own giving history, community calendar, groups, resources, announcements. | Self-management. Joins groups, gives, RSVPs, updates profile. |
| R5 | Attendee / Visitor | Observer | Public calendar, service times, location, welcome content, community highlights. | No decisions. Attends, browses. |
| R6 | Public | Observer | Public website, service times, location. | None. |

**Giving Visibility:** R0-R1 = full giving reports (aggregate and individual). R2 = aggregate for their program only. R3-R6 = hidden. R4 = own giving history only.

### Personal Mode

| Role | Template | Authority | What They See | What They Can Do |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R0 | Owner | Institutional | Everything. This is the same person as R1 in Personal mode. System-level access. | Full system control. |
| R1 | You | Domain Governance | Your entire personal brand. All content, all analytics, all connections, all settings. | Everything. You own your space. |
| R2 | - | - | Not used. Personal mode has no department heads. | - |
| R3 | - | - | Not used. Personal mode has no staff. | - |
| R4 | Subscriber | Personal | Subscriber-only content, direct messaging (if enabled), community feed, exclusive updates. | Self-management. Manages subscription, engages with content. |
| R5 | Follower | Observer | Public content, profile, highlights, public feed. | No decisions. Follows, views, shares. |
| R6 | Public | Observer | Public profile, public content only. | None. |

**Personal Mode Note:** R2 and R3 are intentionally empty. Personal mode is about an individual's brand, not an organization. The jump from R1 (You) to R4 (Subscriber) is by design - there is no middle management in a personal brand.

---

## 5. The Stack

The entire RBAC system reduces to three layers:

**Level -> Role Template -> Screen Experience**

- **Level** (Universal Constitution) = how much power a user has
- **Role Template** (Mode-Specific) = what kind of person they are in that environment
- **Screen Experience** (UI) = what they actually see and do

A Player and a Student can sit on the same universal level (R4 / Level 1 / Personal) but get completely different app experiences because the role template and screen experience are different.

---

## 6. Universal Data Sensitivity Rules

These rules apply across ALL modes:

- **Finance and payment rails:** R0-R2 only (and specific R5 external roles like investors/board with scoped access)
- **Governance and compliance:** R0-R2 only
- **Intelligence (KR, evaluations, scouting):** R0-R2 in Athletics, hidden from R4-R6. R3 sees bands.
- **Personal data (grades, medical, compensation):** Only the individual (R4 self) and authorized leadership (R0-R2 in their lane)
- **Public-facing content (schedule, video, highlights, profiles):** All levels

---

## 7. Dipson RBAC Integration

Dipson enforces RBAC BEFORE assembling any response:

- R0 query: Dipson loads full intelligence + institutional data across all modes
- R1 query: Dipson loads domain-scoped intelligence, strategic data
- R2 query: Dipson loads program-scoped intelligence, competitive data
- R3 query: Dipson loads lane-specific operational data only
- R4 query: Dipson loads self-only data
- R5 query: Dipson responds with community-level information
- R6 query: Dipson responds with public information only

The AI does not have a separate permission level. The AI inherits the permission level of the user asking the question.

---

## Status: LOCKED v2.0

5 modes (Athletics, Business, Education, Community, Personal). 7 universal roles. Mode-specific templates map real-world roles onto the universal ladder. The stack is: Level -> Role Template -> Screen Experience.
